Feng Yuxiang's Circumstances When Leaving Mount Tai 51

Han Was Ordered by Chairman Chiang to Persuade Him to Travel, and Sent a Special Car Prepared for Him to Ride South

Jinan Correspondence, Feng Yuxiang, member of the Central Committee of the Kuomintang, has resided in Mount Tai since the 19th year. During this time, he once entered Chahar, and then returned to Mount Tai, again as a recluse. At first, he lived in the Five Sages Temple, then moved to Xiaowangzhuang, and also founded a primary school to cultivate future generations, advocating sericulture to enrich the people. When free, he indulged in books and sent his thoughts to writing. It has been almost five years since he set foot in the capital. This time, when the Sixth Plenary Session opened, Central Committee members Li Liejun and Chairman Chiang, etc., repeatedly urged him to attend the meeting in Beijing. Chairman Chiang also telegraphed Han Fuqu, chairman of the Shandong Provincial Government, to quickly start the journey. Han complied with the order. After learning about his intentions, he sent Guo Zhigang, advisor to the provincial government, to Taian on the morning of October 31, with a column of armored cars from Jinan, prepared for Feng to ride south. The car included a locomotive, a second-class car, two covered freight cars, and Liu Cunen, deputy captain of the second team of armored cars, with 60 guards, accompanied for protection. At 12:55 noon, they arrived at Taian Station. Guo Zhigang got out of the car, climbed the mountain to visit Feng, and asked about his travel plans. At 6:10 in the afternoon that day, Feng went down the mountain to the station. Those who accompanied Feng included Qiu Shanning, Feng's chief of staff, Zhao Yun, an attendant, and dozens of guards, led by Wei Fenglou. Also present were a messenger, Zhou Bai, the magistrate of Taian County, the director of the business tax bureau, and others who saw him off at the station. A company of soldiers from the 118th Regiment of the garrison was also guarding the station. Feng was wearing a blue cloth jacket and pants, blue socks, and black cloth shoes, with a black felt hunting cap. According to Feng, he said at the station, "I am going to Beijing to attend the Sixth Plenary Session because Chairman Chiang repeatedly telegraphed me to urge me, so I decided to go. At this time of national crisis, and with the urging of all parties, I cannot but go." After speaking, he started the car south at 6:30.

Han Fuju Telegraphs the Central Government Urgently Requesting Funds for Yellow River Bank Closing and Asks for Disaster Relief Bonds to Benefit Disaster Victims 52

Jinan Dispatch: After the plan for closing the Yellow River banks in Shandong Province was finalized, construction of the foundation for both the east and west dams started many days ago. However, due to insufficient funds, essential materials have not been purchased completely. Now that the weather is cold and the water level is low, it is the ideal time to close the banks. Therefore, Han Fuju, Chairman of the Provincial Government, telegraphed the Executive Yuan Economic Commission and Song Ziwen on the 30th, urging them to allocate funds for the bank closure project, stating approximately that 600,000 yuan was needed before November 10th, otherwise credibility would be lost, progress would be impossible, and there would be a risk of suspending work to await materials. Furthermore, considering that the weather is getting colder and the disaster victims urgently need clothing and food, he specifically telegraphed President Wang, Minister Kong, and Xu Shiying of the Relief Committee, requesting the swift issuance of disaster relief bonds with preferential allocation. The telegrams are recorded below: (1) "Respectfully addressed to Wang Jun, President of the Nanjing Executive Yuan: The disaster victims in Shandong Province are gathered and urgently awaiting relief. To cope with the current situation, I previously borrowed 700,000 yuan from banks for relief, which has been reported in a prior telegram. I have also received your esteemed telegram regarding the issuance of 20 million yuan in public bonds, which the Ministry of Finance is planning. I deeply appreciate the central government's concern for the serious disaster and its comprehensive plan for relief, benefiting the surviving population. I should have waited quietly for further instructions without repeated requests. However, millions of people in Shandong Province are crying out for food, and with the severe weather, we must provide both clothing and food to extend their lives. The previous loan has been used for emergency relief and the purchase of cotton clothing and is almost exhausted. Moreover, only one-tenth of the affected people have received this relief, and the number of those who are still suffering is incalculable. The provincial finances are extremely strained, and all resources have been exhausted. The only source of relief funds, such as salary deductions for civil servants and the diversion of land taxes, have been used as collateral for loans. At this critical moment of life and death, there is really no way to provide further assistance. With winter approaching rapidly, there will inevitably be combined suffering from cold and hunger, and people will be wandering everywhere. Not only will I, Fuju, be ashamed before my conscience, but it also seems contrary to the central government's intention to protect its foundation. Your Excellency, your hope is tied to the people, and your benevolence extends to all. I humbly beg you to have compassion for these surviving people and instruct the Ministry of Finance to swiftly issue public bonds and allocate them preferentially to Shandong Province to alleviate their suffering. In urgent anticipation of your orders, I am, your subordinate, Han Fuju, respectfully kowtowing, 30th, confidential civil seal." (2) "Respectfully addressed to the National Economic Commission in Nanjing: I previously received your telegram to continue allocating 200,000 yuan for the bank closing project, which has been handed over to the bank closing committee for use, and I have replied by telegram. However, the cost of purchasing the necessary materials is very high, and the amount previously allocated is far from sufficient. It is estimated that at least 600,000 yuan is needed before the 10th of next month to pay for the materials, otherwise credibility will be lost, progress will be impossible, and there will be a risk of suspending work to await materials. I respectfully request your commission to quickly allocate the funds to meet the urgent need and beg for a telegram in reply. Han Fuju respectfully kowtows, 30th, confidential implementation seal." (3) "Urgent, respectfully addressed to Commissioner Song Ziwen in Shanghai: The Dongzhuang Yellow River bank closing project has been actively prepared for two months. However, the cost of purchasing the necessary materials is very high. The funds previously allocated by the National Economic Commission have been almost exhausted. It is estimated that at least 600,000 yuan is needed before the 10th of next month to pay for the materials, otherwise credibility will be lost, progress will be impossible, and there will be a risk of suspending work to await materials. In addition to telegraphing the Economic Commission to continue allocating funds, I specifically ask my younger brother to instruct them to allocate the full amount as soon as possible to meet the urgent need. Your little brother, Han Fuju, respectfully kowtows, 30th, confidential implementation seal."

The bank closure project in Shandong Province has already started and is expected to be completed by next spring. The people of Juancheng previously submitted a request to the bank closure committee to employ disaster victims in exchange for relief. The engineering team of the committee considered that the affected counties were numerous and located at different distances, making it difficult to implement a uniform regulation. They proposed to limit the scope to the four nearby counties of Heze, Juancheng, Yuncheng, and Juye, and first telegraphed these counties to report the number of able-bodied male disaster victims and formulate work-for-relief measures. At a meeting of the bank closure committee on the 30th, the proposed measures were approved, as follows: (1) The project items, unit price for earthwork, work period, and the number of people required for each project will be determined separately by the committee based on the project conditions. (2) The committee will fairly allocate work based on the distance of each county from the construction site and the number of able-bodied male disaster victims. Disaster victims must not object. (3) Disaster victims must have a complete organization to facilitate command and communication. (4) The committee's supervisors have the right to temporarily increase the number of workers. If there is a risk of delay, the committee may suspend their work. (5) The committee is not responsible for the round-trip travel expenses of disaster victims to and from the construction site. (6) Disaster victims are responsible for building their own shelters. (7) Disaster victims are responsible for providing their own tools for work. (8) Wages will be distributed by the committee's site office to the disaster victim foremen or representatives. (31st)

Songjiang Telephones Requesting Exemption from Transferring Tinglin Water Police

Tinglin Town in the Seventh District of Punan is a prosperous town in our county. Recently, since the Yanggongmiao bandits robbed a car and the Xiahengjing watchtower was robbed of weapons, the local security situation has become increasingly tense. Robbery cases are frequently heard in nearby villages, causing considerable concern among the townspeople. Suddenly, news spread that the Second Platoon of the First Team of the First District of the Waterborne Provincial Public Security Team stationed in Tinglin was to be transferred elsewhere. Everyone believed that the military strength in Tinglin was already extremely weak, and once they were transferred, the people would not be able to sleep peacefully. Therefore, local gentry Liu Jiji, Sun Bokui, Zhou Zhanqi, Jiang Yougu, Tie Jun, Dai Bingjun, Zhou Zhenxian, and others submitted a request to the county government to telegraph the Civil Affairs Department to exempt them from being transferred elsewhere. If a clear order has already been issued, they earnestly request that the order be revoked to maintain security.

Robbery and Injury in Chen Township, Fengbei

Li Dequan's family, located in Group Four, Jia Three, Douchuantan, Chen Township, Fengjing North, was robbed by more than ten bandits on the evening of the 28th of last month. Each bandit carried flashlights and sharp knives. They pried open the front and back doors and first went to the bedroom of his daughter-in-law, Li Yu's. When the woman shouted for help, she was stabbed in the right leg with a sharp knife, causing serious injury. The bandits fled with their loot. Liu Shutang, the head of the Second Sub-bureau, reported to the authorities and immediately rushed to the scene for investigation. He has already reported to the Public Security Bureau for a general search and arrest.

Jiading Jealousy-Motivated Murder and Body Disposal to Destroy Evidence

Zhu Lu's, a widow from Yanjia Temple in the Northwest Township, is 40 years old. She previously hired her cousin, Zhu Zengfu, to farm the land. They lived together day and night and developed an affair. Recently, she changed and hired Gu A'gen, dismissed Zengfu, and then became involved with Gu. Out of jealousy, Zengfu beat Gu with a steel bar one morning on October 4th. As a result, Gu and Zhu Lu's conspired to take revenge. On the night of October 27th, Zengfu was returning home from shopping at Zhujia Bridge. Gu A'tao ambushed him on the way and, taking him by surprise, used a hemp rope to tighten around his neck, dragged him, and hanged him on the triangular wooden frame erected by the nearby Land Survey Team. After he died, they buried him in a peanut field, hoping to destroy the evidence. Zengfu's wife, Shou Shi, noticed that her husband had not returned for several days. She learned that crab catchers had heard cries for help that night, and Gu A'tao had previously threatened to stab Zengfu to death. Knowing that something ominous had occurred, she reported the information to the Loutang Police Station for investigation. Wang Dacheng, the patrol chief of the police station, approved the request and dispatched police to arrest and question Lu's and Gu A'tao. They were sent to the County Public Security Bureau on the first day. Under interrogation by Zhu Cheng, the chief of the Judicial Section, both male and female initially denied the charges. After Zhu Cheng adjourned the court, he devised a way to induce them to confess from the side. Lu's revealed the truth, and the court reopened. Gu A'tao then confessed the aforementioned circumstances. The County Public Security Bureau reported the situation to the county government and instructed the Loutang Police Station to exhume the body north of Yanjia Temple. On the morning of the 2nd, County Magistrate Xu Cixuan, accompanied by officials and police, went to the village to examine the body.

Wuxi Establishes a Winter Defense Office

The county government of our county convened a winter defense conference at 3:00 PM yesterday (the 2nd). Xia Bishu presided over the meeting and decided on the following: (1) Following the precedent of last year, establish a general winter defense office, with two deputy directors. (2) The joint defense districts will remain as they were, with the addition of one deputy director, who will be the head of the local public security sub-bureau or the patrol officer of the directly administered sub-station. (3) The expenses required by the office will be jointly estimated by the security brigade headquarters and the Public Security Bureau, and then submitted to the county for approval by the province. (4) The winter defense office will be officially established on the 10th of this month. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

Changshu A Fire Brigade's Telephone Dispute

The Central District Fire Brigade in our city is affiliated with the Hui Ri Temple but is commercially run and lacks sufficient funds. To facilitate communication, a telephone was installed, connected to a branch line from the Zuijingge Branch Bureau on Temple Front Street. This has been the case for more than three years. The fire brigade also officially registered with the telephone company. Unexpectedly, one night, the telephone company suddenly cut and confiscated the line, and the telephone line of Zuijingge was also cut, causing public outrage. The fire brigade urgently convened a meeting, expressing extreme indignation. All members of the brigade are volunteers, and operating expenses are donated by merchants. The telephone company is also commercially run, and donating and installing free telephones to develop public services is not excessive. However, they have actually taken this action. Three points were immediately proposed and unanimously passed: (1) The telephone switchboard of Zuijingge and the branch switchboard in the brigade will be restored to their original state immediately. (2) Compensation will be paid for damage to the switchboard and telephone lines. (3) Before the matter is resolved, the telephone company will be responsible for all firefighting affairs. The head of the Public Security Bureau was appointed as the mediator that evening.

Nantong The Labor Service Corps Has Been Established

The Nantong New Life Movement Promotion Association's Labor Service Corps was established on the 1st. Xu Zhen and Jin Zonghua were elected as the director and deputy director, respectively. The entire corps is divided into 26 large teams to renovate the city appearance. The general inspection is scheduled for December 1st. They will also promote the movement to wear Nantong homespun cloth to curb social extravagance and regularly hold mass weddings.

Nanjing Central Trust Bureau Handles Insurance for Public Property

The Executive Yuan instructed the Ministry of Finance on October 28th of this year to investigate the Central Trust Bureau's handling of insurance for public property. Please instruct all agencies to open a list of public property and send it to the bureau. After being submitted to the National Government for instructions, it should be approved for implementation. I await your instructions to inform all agencies to investigate, and especially instruct the bureau.

Letter Received

A Humble Suggestion for Salt Administration Reform 53

— Li Youyi

(Continued from Part Two)

(2) Reduce the selling price in various sales areas to benefit the poor. Salt is a necessary food item, especially for the poor, who need it the most, as discussed earlier. Therefore, the selling price should not be too high to burden people's livelihoods. Moreover, the collection of price taxes has a fixed rate (referring to after the standardization of tax rates; if the tax rates vary greatly across the country, there will be excessive or insufficient drawbacks). Transportation costs can also be calculated based on distance. If merchants can obtain a net profit of seven or eight percent annually after all expenses, it seems sufficient. However, today's salt merchants are not like that. According to people in the salt industry, transporting salt from the production areas of Jiangsu Province to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River for sale can yield a net profit of more than one silver dollar per hundred catties (one dan). Their capital is only a little over ten yuan (including salt collection, tax payment, transportation costs, and all other expenses). If one uses 100,000 yuan of capital to transport and sell salt, one can obtain a net profit of more than 10,000 yuan annually, exceeding one percent weekly interest. This is only considering transporting once a year. The enormous profits cannot be ignored. If the government carefully reduces the selling price of salt, taking from the wealth of rich merchants and alleviating the poverty of the poor, the benefits to society would be significant. Merchants, with their large capital, have a substantial profit, so they will naturally be willing to comply. Moreover, salt is a major commodity trade, so the profit margin should be smaller than that of other small-scale businesses. Imposing heavy profits to harm the people is not advisable and is actually the ultimate principle of regulating the social economy. (3) Abolish exclusive merchants, reorganize salt sales regions, and allow people to freely recognize regions for buying and selling, to prevent light eating in remote areas and maintain the business of salt farmers in high-cost salt farms. Everyone knows the drawbacks of exclusive merchants, and abolishing them cannot be delayed, so there is no need to repeat them. As for the permit system, it is intended to make salt transport even and universal, which is not necessarily incorrect. However, the current sales areas were delineated by the previous Qing dynasty. Many years have passed, and the road situation has changed. Moreover, in recent years, rail transportation is vastly different from the past. The government should carefully investigate the salt sales regions set in the past, statistically analyze the production of various farms, examine the distance of roads, allocate salt quotas, reorganize the division of areas, and strive for a balance of supply and demand and suitable transportation. People should be allowed to freely buy and sell within the scope of each region. Then, the worry of light eating in remote areas and the threat of unemployment at high-cost salt farms can both be resolved. (To be continued)

Citizens and the Law (Part 1) 54

(Lectures to the National Public on October 30th and October 1st)

Lin Bin, Member of the Legislative Yuan

Today, the topic I'm discussing is "Citizens and the Law." This topic can be divided into several points. First, let's talk about:

(I) The Meaning of "Citizen" and "People"

A nation is a collective body of human beings. Those who belong to this collective are called "people," and the entire body of people can also be called "nationals." Among the people, some do not have the right to participate in national affairs, while others do. This right to participate in political affairs is called the "right to participate in government." The right to participate in government is a right stipulated and granted to the people under public law, so it is also called "public right." The people who enjoy public rights are citizens. It can be seen that citizens are also people, but they are able to enjoy public rights more than other people.

Being all people of the same nation, why is there such a distinction among them? This is probably because among the people, some are not suitable to participate in government or manage national affairs. Therefore, they are not allowed to have public rights. The laws of various countries have the same intention, and there are often negative qualification restrictions for people who are not suitable to participate in government. Our China has also clearly stipulated this. For example, Article 7, Paragraph 2 of the "Regulations for the Implementation of Township and Town Autonomy" stipulates that those who have one of the following circumstances shall not have the right of citizenship: (1) those who have engaged in counter-revolutionary activities and have been convicted; (2) corrupt officials, unscrupulous bureaucrats, local tyrants, and evil gentry who have been convicted; (3) those who have been deprived of public rights and have not yet been restored; (4) those who are under guardianship; (5) those who use opium or its substitutes. If people have one of these circumstances, they naturally should not be allowed to participate in managing national affairs. Other people who do not have these circumstances may be allowed to have public rights. However, they must also go through a certain procedure. For example, Article 7, Paragraph 1 of the "Regulations for the Implementation of Township and Town Autonomy" stipulates that people of the Republic of China, regardless of gender, who have resided in a township or town area for one year or have a residence there for more than two years, are over 20 years old, and have been sworn in and registered, are township or town citizens and have the right to attend township or town meetings and to exercise the rights of election, recall, initiative, and referendum. According to this provision, people who obtain citizenship must also meet the following requirements: (1) they must be people of the Republic of China; (2) they must have resided in the township or town for more than one year or have a residence there for more than two years; (3) they must be over 20 years old; (4) they must have held the swearing-in ceremony; (5) they must be registered in the citizenship register by the township or town office. People who meet these requirements are township citizens or town citizens, and when a township meeting or town meeting is held, they can attend and exercise the rights of election, recall, initiative, and referendum. These four rights are all political rights, which are the four rights invented by Mr. Sun Yat-sen. People can attend citizens' meetings to exercise these four rights for matters of a county in the locality, and they can also attend the National Assembly or the National People's Congress to exercise these four rights for matters of the central government. This is the function of the so-called right to participate in government. Only citizens have this right, and other people are not allowed to enjoy it according to law. Therefore, there is a distinction between citizens and people. However, in terms of the proportion of the population, those who are not allowed to be citizens because of counter-revolutionary activities and other circumstances are ultimately a very small number. Although it is not possible for everyone to have citizenship in reality, considering the spirit of political participation by all, it is, of course, hoped that no one is not a citizen. Citizens should have a deep understanding of the laws of the country. Other people should also have the same understanding. Whenever there is no need to distinguish between citizens and non-citizens, I will use the word "people" to refer to them collectively. Now I will talk about:

(II) Why Does a Country Need Laws?

To answer this question, we must first divide it into two points: First, what is called a country? Second, what is called a law?

A country is a collective body of human beings, as mentioned above. This collective is different from other collectives. First, it must have a certain population. Second, it must have a certain territory. Third, it must have a certain sovereignty. Any collective of people residing within a certain territory under a single sovereignty is called a country. The number of people can be as few as tens of thousands or as many as hundreds of millions. There is no need for fixed restrictions. The land under the jurisdiction of a country is commonly called territory. Territory indicates the area in which a country exercises its sovereignty. Positively speaking, it can exercise its power over all people within its territory; negatively speaking, it can prohibit other countries from invading its territory and exercising its authority. As for the people, they can be ordered to comply, and at the same time, they are not subject to any power from the outside, which is the manifestation of national power. Therefore, people, territory, and sovereignty are the three elements that constitute a country.

Possessing these elements can be called a country. What is the purpose that a country wants to achieve? In the past, those who advocated individual liberalism believed that the purpose of a country was solely to maintain the personal freedom and property of individuals. However, because the protection of individuals was too thorough, production capital was concentrated in the hands of a small number of people, resulting in inequality in society. Therefore, some people said that the purpose of a country should be based on the interests of all the people, and not focus too much on the protection of individual interests. Modern countries generally follow this view, so the purpose of a country can be divided into four types: (1) Maintaining the survival of the country. To achieve this purpose, all matters related to diplomacy, national defense, and finance should be handled well. (2) Maintaining the security of the country. To achieve this purpose, all matters related to preventing bandits, thieves, and everything that could harm security should be handled well. (3) Defining the boundaries of rights and obligations. The relationship between rights and obligations between individuals or between the state and individuals must be clear to prevent disputes. (4) Promoting the culture of the country. Such as education, health, rescue, industry, transportation, transportation, etc., which are related to the interests of the people and cannot be undertaken by private forces, must be handled by the state. If a country can use these four purposes as its guiding principles for its activities, coordinate class conflicts, and seek the development of common social interests, then it is a good country. If it is the oppression of one class over another and a tool for maintaining the interests of a minority, then it does not conform to the true purpose of the country, and why should there be a country?

Laws can be said to be formulated in order to achieve the goals of the country. What are the goals of the country? People in the past and people today have different views. Therefore, the views on the nature of law are also inconsistent. In the past, those who advocated natural human rights believed that law was a rule that protected individual rights. Today, people believe that law is not to protect individuals, not to protect a certain class, but to maintain the interests of the entire society. This statement is more appropriate. To be more specific, in order to exercise its power, the state should have an organization of organs. The so-called organs can be divided into two types: one is the decision-making organ, where the will of the state is determined by that organ, such as the parliament or the National People's Congress. The other is the executive organ, where the will of the state that has been decided is executed by that organ, such as the monarch of a monarchy, the president of a republic, and other administrative and judicial organs. The organization and powers of these organs are determined by law. If there is no law, the activities of state organs will have no standards. From the perspective of the people, the rights and obligations of the people to the state and the rights and obligations between the people are very complex and must also be regulated by law. If there is no law, the rights of the people will not be guaranteed, and the obligations of the people will have no definite scope. Then, it can be said that the power of the state cannot be exercised and social order cannot be maintained. Therefore, where there is a country, there must be laws. Without laws, the goals of the country can never be achieved. From this, we can see the importance of laws.

There are many types of laws. Those that have been explicitly formulated are called statutory laws, and those that have not been explicitly formulated are called unwritten laws. Those that apply domestically are called domestic laws, and those that apply internationally are called international laws. Those that stipulate the principles for resolving matters are called substantive laws. Those that specify the procedures for applying laws are called procedural laws. The names are inconsistent due to different points of view. It is not possible to explain them in detail at this time. There are also the names of public law and private law. The standards for distinguishing between public law and private law vary among scholars. Some focus on the parties involved in the legal relationship. Any law whose content stipulates the relationship between the state or public groups and individuals is public law. Any law whose content stipulates the relationship between individuals is private law. For example, the constitution, administrative law, criminal law, and procedural law stipulate the relationship between the state and individuals, so they are all public laws. For example, civil law, company law, maritime law, negotiable instruments law, and insurance law stipulate the relationship between individuals, so they are all private laws. Others focus on the nature of the legal relationship as the standard for distinguishing between public law and private law. Any law whose content stipulates a relationship of power and obedience of one party to the other is public law. If it stipulates a relationship of equality between one party and the other, it is private law. These two different statements can only be used as a reference, because in this day and age, there is no absolute distinction between public law and private law. However, for the convenience of research, there are still the terms of public law and private law.

The constitution occupies the most important position in public law. The existence of a country must have a certain population, territory, and administrative organs. The administrative organs must exercise their ruling power for the country. Therefore, the scope of the country's territory, the ethnicity of the country's people, the organization and powers of the country's ruling organs are all explicitly stipulated by law. This type of law is also called the national law in a broad sense. Among them, the constitution stipulates the general principles, and the administrative law stipulates the details. Then, the constitution is the law that stipulates the principles of the organization and scope of activities of the country. The constitution has the strongest effect and is higher than ordinary laws. Laws that conflict with the constitution cannot be considered valid. The constitution cannot be easily amended. The organs and procedures involved in the amendment are also very different from ordinary laws. These two points are the characteristics of the constitution. Modern countries all have constitutions. Our China now has the Provisional Constitution for the Period of Political Tutelage, which is essentially a constitution. When the period of political tutelage expires and the constitutional government begins, there should be a five-power constitution. The draft of this five-power constitution has been drafted by the Legislative Yuan. As long as it is passed by the National Congress of the Kuomintang, it can be submitted for approval at the National Assembly in the future and promulgated for implementation.

Civil law occupies the most important position in private law. Matters such as the relationship between parents, children, siblings, and spouses, the procedures for organizing business groups and establishing legal entities, the relationship between various claims and debts, the state of rights on movable and immovable property, the inheritance of estates, and what kind of behavior can acquire rights and what kind of behavior should bear obligations are all stipulated in detail in the civil law. In the commercial field, such as companies, negotiable instruments, insurance, maritime affairs, banks, and trademarks, separate laws have been formulated, called special civil laws. All civil matters can be handled in accordance with these laws, and if there is a dispute, it can also be resolved in accordance with these laws. It has a close and important relationship with the organization of society and families, the increase of public interests, and the principle of equality between men and women. Most countries have civil laws. Our China has also formulated a civil law of 1,225 articles by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated it for implementation.

The above is the situation in which the state cannot do without laws, and a rough classification of laws. The following will discuss:

(III) The Status of the People in Law

The status of the people in law is different from the past and the present. Recalling the early days of mankind, in order to avoid the harm of poisonous insects and beasts, and to hunt for living materials in the forests and mountains, people had to gather together and seek a common life. The social life at that time was the so-called common labor and common enjoyment. There was no distinction of class, no difference between rich and poor, noble and lowly. Under this natural state of life, how to be equal and how to be unequal did not arise as a question. Later, society gradually developed, and human life progressed from hunting and animal husbandry to agricultural life. As a result, there was also a differentiation of classes in society, and it became a relationship of one class oppressing another class and controlling another class. The phenomenon of inequality became obvious. People who belonged to the dominated class, because of their simple knowledge, still thought that this phenomenon of class domination was natural and should be so. Therefore, they did not feel any dissatisfaction with the phenomenon of inequality. Later, society became more advanced, and human knowledge gradually increased. People had serious doubts about the unequal social phenomenon, thinking that it was caused by the power of the ruling class. Therefore, the call for human equality has spread throughout society since the 17th century. At that time, general natural scholars, such as Locke and Rousseau, further studied the equality rights of human beings and had the so-called theory of natural equality. This theory had a great impact on society at that time. The independence of the United States and the French Revolution in the 18th century were both precedents for breaking the phenomenon of inequality. As for modern times, the constitutions of general countries have provisions for equality rights. In our China, the Provisional Constitution of the Republic of China in the first year of the Republic stipulated the equality of the people in the following words: "The people of the Republic of China are all equal, without distinction of race, class, or religion." The Provisional Constitution for the Period of Political Tutelage of the Republic of China also has such a provision, which reads: "The citizens of the Republic of China are equal in law, regardless of gender, race, religion, or class." Recently, the draft constitution of the Republic of China drafted by the Legislative Yuan has three articles on equality rights. One article states that "the people of the Republic of China are all equal in law." One article stipulates that "all ethnic groups of the Republic of China are constituent elements of the Chinese nation and are all equal." Another article stipulates that "the people of the Republic of China have equal opportunities to receive education." According to these provisions, all citizens, regardless of which ethnic group they belong to, are constituent elements of the Republic of China and are all equal. This is ethnic equality. Regardless of whether they belong to the propertied class or the proletariat, they should receive equal protection or punishment. This is class equality. Regardless of their religious beliefs, they are given equal treatment in law. This is religious equality. Furthermore, regardless of whether they are male or female, except for natural differences due to gender, their treatment in law is also the same. This is equality between men and women. From this, it can be seen that the status of the people in law is equal. All rights that the people can enjoy or obligations that they should bear do not differ due to differences in gender, belief, economic status, etc. As for what are the rights that the people can enjoy and what are the obligations that the people should fulfill, there are also provisions in the law. The following will discuss them separately. (To be continued)

American Vice President Garner and Others Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Morning 55

Met with Mayor Wu for a Luncheon, Finance Minister Kong for a Tea Party in the Afternoon, and a Banquet by Johnson in the Evening; Will Depart for the Philippines This Morning

The delegation of U.S. Congressmen, invited to the Philippines to attend the grand ceremony celebrating the establishment of its independent government, including seventeen senators such as Senator Ashurst, twenty-six congressmen such as Congressman Robertson, and twenty well-known journalists such as Crowning, led by Vice President Garner (John Nance Garner) and Speaker of the House Beane (Joseph B. Byunes), along with their families, a total of 134 people, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning aboard the Dollar Steamship Company's President Grant. They attended a luncheon hosted by Mayor Wu, a tea party hosted by Finance Minister Kong, a banquet hosted by the American Ambassador and the American Consul General, and a tea party hosted by the American community. They boarded the original ship that evening and will depart for the Philippines this morning. Details are as follows:

Welcoming Personnel

Mayor of this city, Wu Tiecheng, represented the Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, the Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Yu Ming, and the representative of the overseas Chinese in the United States, Yang Xichuan, Standing Committee Member of the Kuomintang Branch in the United States. Tan Zhonglu, representative of the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Affairs Bureau of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission. Accompanied by U.S. Ambassador to China Johnson, Consul General to Shanghai Cunningham, U.S. Judge to China Hillermeck, Judge Franklin, Commander of the 4th Marine Regiment in Shanghai, Beaumont, and Major General Kannarb, Colonel Payne, representatives of the American community Biden, Steine, Colin, and Garner's old friend in Shanghai, Fobert, etc. There were also representatives sent by the Philippines to welcome them: Delgado, Gofila, Paksis, Onan, Kachiao, Chaimora, Osmanara, etc., more than twenty people in total. At 7:00 AM, they took a small Dollar Steamship Company ferry from the new customs wharf to the Grant to welcome them. The American welcoming personnel each wore a badge made of red, white, and blue silk on their chests.

Arrival Situation

The Grant had already entered the port at 2:25 AM yesterday morning and was docked at the Dollar Wharf in Zilianjing, Pudong. Garner and others had breakfast on the ship and waited to meet the welcoming personnel. After the American Consul General Cunningham and the special Philippine welcoming representative Delgado delivered welcome speeches, they changed to the Dollar ferry Bopu at 8:00 AM. At 8:30 AM, they arrived at the new customs wharf and disembarked. First, the U.S. Marine Corps dispatched a team to line up on the lawn in front of the new customs wharf to pay their respects. After Garner and Beane disembarked, they were led by Marine Corps Commander Beaumont to inspect the troops. They then went to the Cathay Hotel on the Bund of Nanjing Road to rest.

The Style of the Two Gentlemen

Garner is 63 years old, short and healthy, and full of energy. When he arrived in port yesterday morning, he was wearing a dark blue serge suit, a black woolen overcoat, a light gray felt hat, and black leather shoes. Beane is of similar age, taller, wearing a blue tweed suit, a dark gray felt hat, and black leather shoes and carrying a cane.

Garner's Speech

Garner met with reporters from Chinese and Western newspapers on the ship. According to him, "Our group is only going to Manila to attend the celebration of the establishment of the Philippine government. We have no other mission. We are only stopping by Kobe, Japan, and Shanghai, China, to go ashore for sightseeing. This is purely a private affair." When asked about his views on the future relationship between China, the United States, and the Philippines, Garner declined to comment and said that this was his first visit to the Far East and that he had no mission and should not say much. Garner finally said, "I just read in the newspaper in the living room that President Wang Jingwei of the Chinese government was suddenly assassinated and injured. We are very concerned, but we do not know the details." (Above by New Voice News Agency)

Condolences to Wang

National News Agency Special Dispatch from this city: U.S. Vice President Garner and U.S. Speaker of the House Beane were shocked to hear of President Wang's assassination upon arriving in Shanghai. They immediately sent a telegram from Shanghai to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing to express their condolences. The original telegram read: "We and our delegation are deeply honored to have been received with utmost hospitality by your government. We are deeply saddened to learn of your attempted assassination. Now that we are leaving your country, we wish to reciprocate your kindness and fervently pray for your speedy recovery. (Signed) Vice President Garner, Speaker of the House Beane."

Mayor's Luncheon

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng and his wife, Madam Ma Fengqi, hosted a luncheon at the Shanghai Municipal Government Auditorium yesterday at 1:00 PM to welcome U.S. Vice President Garner, Speaker of the House Beane, and the Congressional delegation. They also invited representatives from all walks of life in Shanghai. Those present included Garner, Beane, seventeen U.S. Senators such as Ashurst, twenty-six Congressmen such as Robertson, and twenty American journalists such as Crowning, as well as their families, totaling over 100 people. The guests included U.S. Ambassador Johnson, Consul General Cunningham, Judge Hillermeck, Commercial Counselor Arnold, Chinese Minister to France Gu Weijun, Yu Ming, Zheng Lai, Dong Xian Guang, Guo Dehua, Xu Xinliu, Yu Qiaqing, Bei Songsun, Du Yuesheng, Wang Xiaolai, Guo Bingwen, Ma Yinliang, Li Cai, Qian Cangshi, Liang Shichun, Xu Jianping, Yang Guangheng, Tang Liangli, Wen Wanqing, and various bureau chiefs and secretaries of the municipal government, totaling over 200 people. There were 24 tables, with nine people at each table. The meal was Chinese cuisine prepared by Xinghualou Restaurant, and the Public Concession Band played music to entertain the guests. Halfway through the meal, Mayor Wu stood up, raised his glass, and wished Vice President Garner, Speaker Beane, and all the congressmen good health. Both Garner and Beane also stood up to return the toast and thanked him in their speeches. They parted happily at around 3:00 PM. After the luncheon, a group photo was taken in front of the city government gate to commemorate the occasion. (Central News Agency)

Finance Minister Kong's Tea Party

From 4:30 PM to 6:30 PM, Executive Yuan Vice President and Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi and his wife held a grand tea party at the Paramount Ballroom on Yuyuan Road, inviting Song Ziwen, Standing Committee Member of the National Economic Council, Mayor Wu, Dr. Wang Zhengting, and the American Ambassador, American Consul General, American Commercial Counselor, and hundreds of Chinese and American officials and leaders from all walks of life in Shanghai to attend.

Departure for the Philippines This Morning

At 8:15 PM, the American Ambassador and Consul General hosted a banquet at the International Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road, also inviting Finance Minister Kong, Mayor Wu, Director Yu, and Secretary-General Yu, and other Chinese officials to attend. From 10:30 PM to 11:30 PM, Garner and others continued to meet with American expatriates in Shanghai on the third floor of the hotel and held a tea party. They then boarded the original ship from the new customs wharf at 1:30 AM that night. The American Ambassador and American Consul General went to the wharf to see them off. At 4:45 AM this morning, they set sail from Shanghai, passed the port, and headed for the Philippines, spending less than 24 hours in Shanghai. They plan to stop in Shanghai for a longer period of time on their return trip.

Garner's Brief Biography

Garner has been prominent in American politics for more than 43 years. He was born in the Red River area on the Rio Grande border in Texas. At the age of 20, he served as a state advisor. Twenty years later, he was promoted to Congressman. In 1931, he was elected Speaker of the House of Representatives. In 1932, he was elected to his current position, with a term from 1933 to 1937. (Above by New Voice News Agency)

Philippine Representative's Speech

Chairman of the Philippine Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission, Delgado, delivered a welcome speech to the country after meeting with Garner. "U.S. Vice President Garner, Speaker of the House Beane, and the American press delegation have been invited by the Philippine government to attend the celebration of the establishment of the new Philippine government on the 15th of this month (November). This is enough to show the friendship between the people and governments of the United States and the Philippines. On the other hand, this invitation has a profound meaning. The Philippine government and people hope that they will get to know the administrative legislators who will reform Philippine affairs with the new government and understand the administration of the new government personnel in the Far East and on the island. As a result, the new government personnel will have convenience in legislation in the future. Garner et al. will not only travel to various parts of the Philippines, but also go to China and Japan for sightseeing. The inauguration ceremony of the new Philippine government personnel will be at the time of the establishment of the new government. After the new government personnel are guided by Garner et al., the Philippine government can consolidate its friendly relations between the major countries on both sides of the Pacific Ocean. The Philippine government and I sincerely celebrate the health of the National Government of China, the Shanghai Municipal Government, and the Chinese people." (New News Agency)

Silver Senator's Remarks

The Great American Evening Post reported that the famous American "Silver Senators" Wheeler and King arrived in Shanghai today (2nd) with U.S. Vice President Garner. They told news reporters that the American silver purchasing policy will continue. King even said that he expects the price of American silver to rise to US$1.29 per ounce. Wheeler claimed that he could not elaborate on the U.S. silver policy in a few minutes, but two points could be confirmed: the current policy will continue, and this policy is beneficial to the United States. The reason can be found in his speech on the issue. As for the sudden and tragic fall of the Shanghai silver dollar when the price of silver is still high, it should be known that Shanghai cannot be considered as China now. The American silver group is still seeking to recoin silver coins according to the ratio of 16 to 1 of the bimetallic standard. Managed currency is sufficient to cause a very harmful currency war. The way to avoid it is that the currency is based on metal. Now that there is insufficient gold in the world as a metal base, silver should also be used to assist it. He predicted that the currencies of major countries will restore the metal base. As for when it will be realized, it cannot be determined. Wheeler plans to stay in China for a short time when he returns from the Philippines to investigate the current situation of silver. However, the scope of the investigation will be determined temporarily. Wheeler visited China in 1927. Senator King also said that the silver policy is beneficial to the United States, but he could not elaborate on the reason due to the lack of time. He also said, "I know the impact of American silver purchases on China. Frankly speaking, most of the silver we purchase comes from China, but China should find a way to solve its own problems." In the past, King had a great influence on the United States' recognition of the National Government.

Simple Life Insurance Will Be Implemented on the First of Next Month 57

Postal Districts in Various Places Will Continue to Handle the Business Next March; Office Staff Were Recruited Yesterday for Training

Shiye News Agency reported that the simple life insurance organized by the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of the Ministry of Communications will be implemented in Shanghai, Nanjing, and Hankou starting from the first of next month without delay. Fifteen office staff were specially recruited yesterday for training. Details are as follows:

Scheduled Implementation

The simple life insurance law of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval by the Ministry of Communications, and 500,000 yuan of tomb money has been allocated to develop the business. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau and the Nanjing-Hankou Branch have decided to implement it starting from the first of next month. Yesterday, an order from the National Government said, "The Simple Life Insurance Law will be implemented starting from December 1, 1935. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau and the Nanjing-Hankou Branch will first open insurance business. The postal districts of Shanghai, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan will, starting from March 1, 1936, handle the business separately according to the situation. This order."

Recruiting Clerks

The bureau specially advertised to recruit 15 clerks yesterday for training because simple life insurance is a new creation. Details are listed below: (1) Number: 15 for official and 15 for standby; (2) Qualifications: A. Graduates of public or registered private senior high schools, old-style middle schools, or other equivalent schools with certificates; B. Those with equivalent academic ability as senior high school or old-style middle school graduates who have passed the general examination; (3) Age: Under 30; (4) Written examination subjects: A. Party principles; B. Chinese; C. English; D. General business knowledge; E. Mathematics; F. Basic bookkeeping knowledge; (5) Registration location: Ministry of Communications; (6) Registration time: From November 1 to 15; (7) Registration fee: One yuan; (8) Registration procedures: Submit proof documents and two recent 2.5-inch half-length photos; (9) Examination location: Ministry of Communications; (10) Examination date: Starting from November 20; (11) Treatment: After being admitted through the examination, there will be a trial period of six months, with a monthly salary of 30 to 40 yuan. After the trial period expires, those who pass the assessment will be added to the formal staff of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau.

Most of the Rumors in the Market Are Inaccurate; The Municipal Authorities Strictly Suppress Them; Those Who Create Rumors Will Be Subjected to Military Law 58

Central News Agency reported that the exchange transactions of various exchanges have been fluctuating recently, and rumors have been spreading, causing public anxiety. In order to understand the truth, reporters inquired about the news from various parties of the authorities. The results showed that the reason for the recent fluctuations in various exchanges was actually caused by those who deliberately manipulate them for speculation and profit. The government has always adopted a prudent policy and has not taken any action. Moreover, the general national economy has been relatively good recently, and there are no difficulties in the financial situation. All kinds of rumors are inaccurate. The fact that the Central Bank stabilizes foreign exchange is particularly obvious. It is hoped that people will no longer be fooled by those who create rumors.

Suppressing Absurd Rumors

Central News Agency reported that the securities, gold, and grain markets in this city experienced chaos on the afternoon of the first day due to the news of the assassination of Executive Yuan President Wang Jingwei. However, all three bullets that President Wang was hit were not fatal, and he recovered well after the surgery. The Sixth Plenary Session was still held as usual. Therefore, after the opening of the various exchanges yesterday morning, they all returned to the state of the previous few days, and all securities rose. The municipal authorities are strictly suppressing all kinds of absurd rumors from the outside world.

Three Rumor Creators Arrested

Central News Agency reported that evil people in this city spread rumors. The Municipal Government ordered the Public Security Bureau to investigate and deal with the matter strictly. Recently, the Municipal Government was informed that the rumors were organized, and their purpose was to confuse people's minds and disrupt the market. It was also heard that the Public Security Bureau has arrested three rumor creators. Mayor Wu has ordered them to be handed over to the military law department of the garrison headquarters for strict investigation and punishment.

Cai Jingjun's Speech

A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Cai Jingjun, Director of the Public Security Bureau, yesterday to ask about the public security situation in this city due to the many rumors. He replied that the bureau is responsible for maintaining public security in accordance with the mayor's instructions. It usually contacts the police authorities in the concessions to cooperate in clearing out reactionary elements and eliminating petty thieves. Therefore, although the market is very depressed, it can still be safely passed. Recently, the winter prevention season is approaching. The bureau has convened various branches and teams to prepare early in reference to the successful cases of winter prevention in previous years. Therefore, even if there are evil people spreading rumors in the market these days, they have not only failed to use their skills, but also been arrested by our long police yesterday. They are being interrogated severely and will be severely punished. I hope that the citizens will remain calm and not be confused by rumors. This is the most important thing.

We cannot bear the eagerness to await orders, and we respectfully submit to the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Executive and Supervisory Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang, Shanghai Low Rent Association, Winter,"

Compilation of the Main Text

Central News Agency reported that since the Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee launched the rent reduction campaign, it has been more than two years. Although efforts have been made to appeal, the owners have not understood the depression of the market and have maintained their prejudices to the extent that they have not been popularized. Although a small number of owners have been considerate of the difficulties of the merchants and have voluntarily reduced the rent, they are all in remote corners of the city. Therefore, there are countless lawsuits. In order to reduce the burden on citizens, the association has specially appointed volunteer lawyers to defend all sectors of society in court and obtain legal relief. In order to make all citizens in the city understand the rent reduction steps and legal procedures, the recent court judgments on rent reduction and the negotiations between the owners and tenants have been compiled into a booklet for reference by all sectors of society. Once the market situation improves, the original state will be restored. It is also heard that the association has a volunteer legal team, and rent reduction cases can be legally protected. This afternoon at 2:00 PM, the association was notified by the Shanghai Rent Reduction Federation to convene a joint meeting of the rent reduction branches of all districts of the city at the Hai Ning Road Nan Lin Li Minsheng Primary School. All branches in the South District can send three members to participate.

Sudden Increase in Overseas Sales of Chinese Silk: Prices Rise More Than Double, but Raw Material Shortages Force Some to Halt Production 63

According to the New Voice News Agency, the overseas trade of Chinese silk has been greatly reduced due to the dumping of Japanese silk in European and American markets, resulting in a sharp drop in silk prices and silk merchants teetering on the brink of bankruptcy. Now, since autumn, overseas sales of Chinese silk have gradually improved, and silk prices have soared. Raw materials in various regions are about to be exhausted. Details are as follows:

Improvement in Overseas Sales

Overseas sales of Chinese silk have been sluggish for years. B-grade silk has fallen to below 400 national currency yuan per picul, a rare occurrence. Silk reeling is bound to lose money, making it impossible for silk factories and merchants in Jiangsu and Zhejiang to maintain operations, and they are on the verge of bankruptcy. In Shanghai, out of 113 single and double palace silk factories, only about one-tenth can barely maintain operations. Since the autumn of this year, Chinese silk has suddenly become active in European and American markets, and foreign firms stationed in Shanghai are purchasing Chinese silk, which has caused silk prices to rise slightly. B-grade silk has risen to about 500 national currency yuan per picul, and silk factories have also started operations one after another.

Soaring Silk Prices

Exports of Chinese silk gradually increased in July, August, September, and October, and by October, they had returned to their previous state. Prices have also risen accordingly. B-grade silk currently costs 840-850 national currency yuan per picul, more than double the previous price, which has not been seen since 1930. Silk factories and merchants in various regions have made large profits. It is said that Yongtai in Wuxi and Baotai in Shanghai are the largest. At the same time, cocoons and waste materials have also risen in price. The number of silk factories starting operations has suddenly increased, and exports of double palace silk are also gradually booming. The Fulun Heng Double Palace Factory on Tianbao Road in Hongkou has also leased the Honglun Double Palace Factory on Liuying Road in Zhabei to start operations.

Raw Material Shortages

Farmers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang have seen the decline in overseas sales of Chinese silk, which has led to a sharp drop in silk prices. Cocoon prices have fallen to about 20 national currency yuan per picul. Each time they raise silkworms, there is no profit to be made, so they have to convert mulberry fields to grow other agricultural products, which has greatly reduced cocoon production. Since the autumn of this year, after the improvement in overseas sales of Chinese silk, there has been a significant shortage of raw materials. Silk factories with smaller capital have been forced to stop production due to lack of raw materials.

Sea Defense Liner "Haiyi" Ship Faces Navigation Issues; Hong Kong Government Nitpicks International Safety Certificate 64

The "Haiyi" ship was newly purchased from abroad and has a very large load capacity. Although the ship is relatively old, the construction is still very solid. Previously, at the request of sugar merchant Zheng Zenan and others, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company (招商局) was entrusted with transporting goods in Beihai, Haikou, and Sanbu, so it was agreed with the Chinese merchants to operate the "Haiyi" ship on the Shanghai-Fangcheng route, carrying passengers at the same time. However, when passing through Shantou and Hong Kong, it was necessary to apply for three documents, including an international safety navigation certificate and a radio certificate, before the Hong Kong government would allow it to carry passengers in and out. At the time of the maiden voyage, after various negotiations, the certificate was finally obtained. The international navigation safety certificate for Chinese seagoing vessels, in addition to the China Merchants’ "Four New" ships, only this "Haiyi" ship possessed it.

Failure to Pass Re-Inspection

Unexpectedly, when the "Haiyi" arrived in Hong Kong, the Hong Kong government verified the safety certificate but required a re-inspection to determine whether it met the various conditions listed on the safety certificate. After the Hong Kong government sent a surveyor to inspect the "Haiyi" ship, it was discovered that there were only sampans on the deck, not lifeboats, and the life jackets on board were also deemed insufficient. Other items such as the deck and cabins did not conform to the international navigation safety certificate. Therefore, they were nitpicking and unwilling to compromise. As a result, the "Haiyi" was deemed not suitable for navigating international ports and carrying passengers and could only be used as a cargo ship.

Major Repairs Require Huge Expenses

After this re-inspection, the Hong Kong government refused to issue a passenger license, which meant that it could not operate at various seaports abroad. If it was necessary to continue sailing, major repairs would have to be carried out, and the instructions of the Hong Kong government's surveyor had to be followed. The repairs had to be carried out at a Hong Kong shipyard, but according to the major repair plan set by the Hong Kong government, the required repair costs and various modifications would cost at least 100,000 yuan. Currently, the Chinese Merchant Shipping Company is still considering this.

Central Cooperative Research Class: Visiting Group Arrived in Shanghai from Suzhou Yesterday; Visited Shanghai Today and Will Go to Hangzhou Tonight; The Group Published Their Impressions of the Inspection Along the Way 68

The Cooperative Research Class of the Organization Committee of the Central Party Headquarters, in order to observe the actual experience of cooperative enterprises in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, specially organized a visiting group to conduct on-site inspections in the Jiangsu and Zhejiang areas. The group consisted of more than 30 members, led by Chen Zhongming as the general leader. They departed from Nanjing on the Beijing-Shanghai train on October 27th. They passed through Zhenjiang, Wuxi, Suzhou, and Zhenze, and got off the train to visit various places. On November 1st, after visiting the Guangfu Cooperative Experimental Zone in Wuxian County, they took a train to Shanghai to inspect cooperative enterprises. Details are as follows:

Visiting Shanghai Today

The group first sent Tang Naixin, a member of the public relations section, to Shanghai the night before last to make arrangements. Yesterday morning, the entire group of more than 30 members, led by the general leader, arrived in Shanghai. After contacting party, government, and educational institutions, they decided to depart this morning to visit the Yutang Cooperative in Shanghai County. Tomorrow morning or tonight, they will go to Hangzhou and then to Jiaxing and Huzhou to visit. They are scheduled to return to Nanjing from Hangzhou via the Beijing-Hangzhou National Highway on the 6th.

Cooperative Conditions in Various Places

Chen Zhongming, the general leader of the group, talked about the conditions of cooperative enterprises in various places yesterday: (1) Zhenjiang Xin'an Credit Guarantee Cooperative is the only new-style credit cooperative in Jiangsu Province. At the beginning of its establishment, it was due to the advocacy of Mr. Jin Zhiren, the business director of the Bank of China in Zhenjiang. Therefore, its capital operation relies heavily on the Bank of China. The guarantee liability of the cooperative is only three times the amount of the shares. The members are very enthusiastic about the cooperative affairs. If they can further adapt to training, improve their various knowledge, and consider increasing their guarantee liability, so that it can be guided by the organization and then operated independently, its future development is limitless. (2) Wuxi Chaomi Bang Rickshaw Utilization Cooperative and Consumer Cooperative are both established under the guidance of the Jiangsu Provincial Educational Institute and the Public Education Hall. The rickshaw cooperative has 20 members and currently has 10 vehicles. The members take turns pulling the rickshaws, and they are full of vitality. The funds for purchasing the vehicles were borrowed from private individuals who are enthusiastic about cooperation. However, private power is ultimately limited, and local financial institutions, especially the Farmers Bank, should not shirk their responsibility to encourage and promote them. In addition, due to the difficulty of purchasing vehicle licenses, the number of members in the cooperative cannot be increased. However, for the sake of development, it is advisable to add probationary members and try to add new vehicles. On the one hand, prepare for the situation where members cannot pull the rickshaws due to other matters, so as to avoid the malpractice of temporarily finding non-members to pull the rickshaws. As for the establishment of the consumer cooperative, although it has been less than a month, the results are quite impressive. If it is possible to find ways to directly connect with producers in terms of purchasing goods, its business will be more progressive. (3) Kai Xian Gong Raw Silk Refining, Transportation, and Sales Cooperative has a long history of struggle. Although it has suffered a lot of losses due to the drop in silk prices, it can still cope with the difficulties and repay the loans. The processing part of the cooperative is undertaken by the family members of the members, and their spirit is also very good. (4) Guangfu Cooperative Experimental Zone was originally jointly organized by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction and the China Cooperative Society. It has been operating for several years with little success. On July 1st of this year, the Jiangsu Provincial Government specially entrusted the China Cooperative Society to fully design and guide it. After the China Cooperative Society took over, it organized a guidance committee for the experimental zone, and under it, it established a design committee and implemented rectification matters. The original 23 silkworm raising cooperatives have been sorted out and are now undergoing the reorganization of the joint cooperative. The day the group visited happened to be the day the joint cooperative held its representative conference. There were 105 member representatives and a small number of peasant women serving as representatives. The hardship, difficulty, simplicity, and longing of the representatives can truly express the suffering of the entire Chinese countryside and the need for cooperative enterprises.

City Chamber of Commerce Sends Another Telegram Requesting Strict Prohibition of Shaoxing Deducting Foreign Exchange Premiums on Central Bank Notes 70

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent another telegram yesterday to the Ministry of Finance and the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting that the Shaoxing money industry be stopped from deducting foreign exchange premiums on banknotes issued by the Central Bank and other banks. The telegram stated: (Title omitted) On the 1st of this month, the Foil Industry Association sent a letter stating that in the reply from your association on August 10th, No. 2920 of Pu Zi, it was mentioned that the Shaoxing money industry was deducting premiums on banknotes issued by the Central Bank and other banks. The Ministry of Finance was requested to stop it. On the 10th of this month, the Ministry of Finance issued a reply, No. 6606 of Qian Zi, which stated that they had received the telegram and had instructed the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance to instruct the Shaoxing County Government to investigate and strictly prohibit it. The letter was recorded and notified to all members of our association. Now, according to reports from members of our association, the Shaoxing money industry has dared to defy the orders of the Ministry and still deducts the premium (secretly called foreign exchange premium) of 17 or 18 yuan per thousand yuan of banknotes issued by the Central Bank and other banks from the industry when they go to Shaoxing to purchase goods. It has been more than a month since the premium was raised to more than 20 yuan. Observing the current situation, it will gradually rise in the future. Since June of this year, the industry has suffered additional losses due to the foreign exchange premium. Please send another telegram to the Ministry of Finance to fight for it. Accordingly, the affiliated association has re-examined and verified the facts. The facts are hereby conveyed. We respectfully request your association to forward it to the Ministry of Finance and the Zhejiang Provincial Government Department of Finance, and strictly order the Shaoxing County Government to investigate and prohibit the deduction of foreign exchange premiums on banknotes issued by the Central Bank and other banks, so as to maintain national law and avoid additional losses for merchants. The attendees checked the matter and found that it had been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for instructions to prohibit it. Now, according to the report from the association, the local money industry not only resists orders as before, but also increases the foreign exchange premium. This is foolish for the national law and increases the burden on merchants. Once this example is set, there will be no end to it. The monetary system is concerned, and it should not be allowed to be perfunctory. We should send a telegram to the Ministry and the Provincial Government for review and approval, and strictly order the local government to stop it, which is for the public good. Shanghai Koutou.

Zhenwu Commissioner of the Red Swastika Society Reports on the Disaster Situation in Northern Jiangsu 71

The Red Swastika Society believed that the flood disaster in northern Jiangsu was severe, and had publicly appointed Zhenwu Commissioners Chen Wangqiu, Zhu Weiyi, Tang Fuyun, and Liu Foyuan to go to various counties in Xuhai to investigate the disaster situation, and at the same time raise Zhenkuan (relief funds) to prepare for the purchase of grain and medicine to be transported to the disaster area for relief. It is now heard that the Zhenwu Commissioner of the office has personally gone to various disaster areas to conduct on-site investigations of the disaster situation, and has submitted a detailed report, which is recorded as follows: Pei County is 120 li (Chinese miles) away from Tongshan, connected to the northern Jiangsu levee. When the levee broke, the county was the first to bear the brunt. Initially, the second district was flooded, and then the flood spread to five districts. The flood came suddenly, and the people were caught off guard, and countless people were drowned. On the 26th and 27th, there was wind and rain, and the flood rushed straight to the northeast earthen city of the county, which was extremely dangerous. The east, west, and north gates were blocked to prevent water from pouring in, leaving only the south gate for access. Now, the waves are surging, and there is no end in sight. Transportation is cut off. Xun and others had to turn back midway. Pi County: On the 29th, they took the Longhai train to Pi County to investigate. When the train arrived at Daxu Station, they saw that the north of the railway was flooded with several feet of water. After advancing several li, the Tongshan boundary merged with Pi County, and the north and south of the railway were flooded. Villages were submerged, and houses in high places were trapped in the water. Houses in low places collapsed and flowed away with the waves. The scene was so tragic that it made people's hearts ache. From Daxu east to Pao Station, heading north for 156 li, the north and south of the railway were boundless. From Yunhe Station to Guanhu Town, advancing by land and water, they finally reached the county seat. The county is divided into seven districts. The disaster situation in the third, fourth, and fifth districts is the most serious, followed by the sixth district, and then the first and second districts. There is no disaster in the seventh district. Many disaster victims have fled. The county has set up two shelters, one on the Gaogang in the north of the city and the other on Suyang Mountain. There are about 3,000 refugees who have not been taken in. They are all temporarily built thatched huts. The disaster victims are all emaciated. Usually, the people of the county mostly eat red grain. Even the third-class noodles are regarded as treasures. When they returned along the original road, they took a train to Xinpu, and it was already late at night. Donghai County: Because the water at Wuhua Bridge rose and the Wanggong River levee broke, the towns in the second district were completely submerged. The first district, from Xiapu to Dapu Xinpu, and the area south of the railway, became a swamp, 30+ li wide from southeast to northwest and 120+ li long from north to south. There are about 20,000 disaster victims. Guanyun County: The areas around Daxiao Luhuzhuang in the second district of the county, as well as the Honggou Chekou Daxiao Maozhuang area in the first district, to Fenghuang Town, are all flooded. The disaster victims have no clothes and no food, and the situation is too terrible to witness. Shuyang County: Due to the turbulent water at Liu Lao Jian, the ninth district, from Yangkou to Machang, is about 20+ li from east to west, and from Wuji to Zhou Shenji in Lianshui County is about 50+ li from north to south, with several feet of water. It is still rising. The above counties have been personally investigated. Suqian and Lianshui in Huaishu, and Feng County in Xushu, have not yet been investigated. For this Zhenwu, Xia Pi and Pei County should be started from in Xushu, and Shuyang should be started from first in Haishu. Red grain should be used for Zhen in Xushu, and taro rice should be used for Zhen in Haishu. Both can be purchased in the respective counties. Red grain costs about 4 yuan per market dou cao, which is 150 jin (Chinese pounds) per dan. Corn costs about 3.5 yuan per 100 jin. It is now autumn, and the disaster victims are suffering from hunger and cold. Winter is coming soon, and there is a risk of freezing and starvation. I sincerely hope that the general office will make a call to action, awaken the sympathy of all sectors, and provide benevolent syrup and righteous grain to save the dying disaster victims. I bow my head nine times to ask for the lives of the disaster victims.
