It is reported that the Ministry of Communications has instructed the Shanghai Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau to provide a preferential compensation of 400 yuan each to the families of the deceased Yuan Bingshu, the stack clerk, and Lu Ruilin, the guard, who died in the line of duty, in accordance with the postal bureau's compensation regulations.

Xu Renguang Narrowly Escapes Abduction 73

Incident Occurs in Cihui Nanli; Brown Car Used with Forged License

Xu Renguang, a native of Huzhou, is 36 years old and lives at 24 Jin Shenfu Road in the French Concession. His sister, Xu Renyi, is the principal of the Zhirenyong Girls' School in this city. Some time ago, Xu Renyi went abroad to study, so she entrusted the school affairs to Xu Renguang to manage. Renguang had a new-style Henderson sedan, license number 5116, which he drove himself, using it as transportation every morning to go to the school for work. Yesterday morning around 9 a.m., Xu drove to the school. Because Weihaiwei Road near the corner of West Miller Road, near the school, was under construction and vehicles were prohibited from passing, he changed his route and drove into Cihui Nanli. He got out of the car in the last lane of the lane. Just as Xu was getting out of the car, a brown old sedan was parked next to the last lane, with three people in the car. One seemed to be a driver, and the two men were sitting in the back, wearing gray robes. As soon as they saw Xu Renguang getting out of the car, the two men jumped out of the old car at the same time, blocking Xu's path. They took out handguns, warned him not to make a sound, and forcibly dragged Xu into the brown car. At that time, Xu Renguang knew that he had encountered bandits. Knowing that he could not resist, he had no choice but to obey and get into the car. The bandit in the front drove the car out of the lane and headed west on Foch Road. At the same time, the bandits took out a pair of black glasses and ordered Xu to put them on his nose. Before long, the car arrived at the intersection of Avenue Albert and Rue Massenet. The bandits suddenly said to Xu, "You have to go to Rue Poncet to see our commander." They ordered the bandit driving the car to turn and head towards Rue Poncet. When they arrived at the intersection, the car stopped. The two bandits then pushed Xu out of the car. Just as he was about to step down, Xu Renguang saw that the bandits' guard was slightly lax. He desperately jumped out of the car and ran wildly, shouting kidnapping and help along the way. At that time, there were many people coming and going on the road. The bandits, seeing that the matter had been exposed, dared not chase him. They hurriedly jumped into the bandit car and fled west. By the time the Yue patrol officer No. 609 nearby heard the alarm and arrived, it was too late. He escorted Xu Renguang back to the police station. But at this time, the French police had already received a report from the Jing'an Temple Police Station of the Public Concession. When Xu Renguang was kidnapped, it happened to be seen by a Zhu surname tenant in No. 22, who recorded the bandit's car license plate as 4753 and reported it to the police station by telephone. Therefore, after Xu reported the incident, the Jing'an Temple Police Station sent a detective to take Xu back, inquired in detail about the bandits' clothing and appearance, sent him back to his residence, and notified the city's police agencies to track down the car. Until around 11 a.m., the car was discovered by a patrolling western police officer at the intersection of Jing'an Temple Road and Tongfu Road. There was no one in the car. He returned to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, drove the car into the police station, carefully examined the traces in the car, took photos for file, and investigated the car license result. It was discovered that it was a forgery. At the same time, it is still under investigation whether the car was robbed by the bandits.

Zhabei: Daylight Robbery at Huang Yichu's Home on Ouyang Road 74

The security team police engaged in a fierce battle with the bandits, resulting in the capture of three bandits alive and the killing of one. They seized one pistol and seven bullets. The homeowner's estimated loss is over 10,000 yuan.

Yesterday around 10:00 AM, a major robbery occurred at the home of Huang Yichu, a Cantonese tea merchant, located at No. 10 Ouyang Road, Zhabei. The loss is estimated to be over 10,000 yuan. Details are as follows:

Circumstances of the Incident: Huang Yichu, a tea merchant from Guangdong, purchased land on Ouyang Road, under the jurisdiction of the Linping Road Police Station in Zhabei, and built a Western-style house. It was surrounded by bamboo fences and had a small garden, making it exquisite and beautiful. Recently, Huang returned to Guangdong for business, and his son, Ke Ming, also went to Hankou for business. Only six or seven people, including women, children, and maids, were left at home to guard the property. Unexpectedly, around 10:00 AM yesterday, Huang Yichu's wife, Fan Changdi (i.e., Mrs. Huang Fan), went out to buy food. Suddenly, three bandits in Western suits and one bandit in a Zhongshan suit, a total of four, claiming to have come from Nanjing to Shanghai to see Mr. Huang, broke into the living room. The three bandits drew their pistols and drove all the women, children, and maids into the west wing, tying them up one by one with ropes. Two bandits held guns to scare them and prevent them from making noise, monitoring their movements. The other two bandits went upstairs, rummaging through boxes and chests, looting all valuables and escaping.

The Pursuit and Capture of the Bandits: When the bandits went to rob, the newspaper delivery man had not yet arrived. The bandits pulled the wire bell outside the fence for a long time, but no one opened the door. At that time, Qu Huaili and Chi Wuqin, squad leaders of the Fifth Team of the Shanghai North District Security Corps, happened to see this and secretly suspected something. However, they dared not do anything. After the bandits entered the house, they heard the sound of a child crying inside, increasing their suspicion. Still, they dared not act rashly. Chi rushed back to the team to report to Deputy Team Leader Song Shouming. However, the location was about two miles away from the Fifth Team headquarters. After receiving the report, Song instructed Chi to rush to report to the Jixiang Road Police Station under their jurisdiction. Meanwhile, Song led the team members to the scene, arriving around 10:45 AM. The bandits had been searching for about an hour and were leaving. At this time, Qu heard shouts from inside and realized that they were indeed robbers. After the four bandits left the house, they fled wildly towards the countryside of Quanjiazhai. Qu chased after them, and the bandits fired their pistols along the way as they fought and fled. By the time they reached Quanzhai, one bandit had run out of bullets and threw his pistol into the river, surrendering. At this time, Fang, an officer from the Jixiang Road Police Station, and Niu, the director of the Linping Road Police Station, arrived one after another, returning fire. The sound of gunfire continued incessantly as they chased for five or six miles. One bandit stood his ground to fight at the former Liu Family Residence, but Qu dodged into a nearby manure pit and shot the bandit in the back. The bullet exited through the front chest, and the bandit could not stand and fell into the riverbank. Qu rushed forward and seized a six-inch nine-shot Browning pistol, serial number 260, with seven bullets remaining. Another bandit was also captured, but he had discarded his pistol along the way. In total, three bandits were captured alive, and one was killed. A portion of the stolen jewelry was recovered and handed over to the Jixiang Road Police Station, along with the people and the loot, and transferred to the Linping Road Police Station.

Names of the Bandits: The bandits captured alive are Chen Biao, 28 years old; Wu Chunshan, 25 years old; both claiming to be from Hunan. The other bandit is Chen Hongsheng, 24 years old, from Hangzhou. The bandit who was killed was named Wang Ying, 24 years old, from Ningbo. The deceased was wearing a blue serge Western suit, a yellow shirt, and dancing leather shoes. There were four characters written horizontally on his chest: "Class B 26". There was another four-character phrase that looked like "athlete". The police station under their jurisdiction has instructed the local bailiff to report to the Shanghai District Court for an autopsy.

List of Lost Items: (1) Two jade bracelets, two pearl rings with diamonds, three jade rings, one jade bead, two jade buttons, one jade brooch, one gold pocket watch, over two hundred pearls, over ten loose jade beads, one ruby ring, one gold ring with a name engraved on it, ten yuan in paper money, three yuan in cash, and six jiao in small bills. (2) Three pairs of gold earrings, two wristwatches, one pair of diamond drop earrings, one pair of pearl earrings, one pair of ruby earrings, two pairs of emerald earrings, two diamond rings, one pearl ring, one ruby ring, two emerald rings, one emerald brooch, three jade and emerald beaded bracelets, four gold bracelets, four gold rings, two pairs of silver chopsticks, one pair of diamond earrings, etc. All of the above items were stolen from the rooms of Huang Fan and Fan's daughter-in-law, Guo Qing (i.e., Mrs. Huang Guo).

Aviation Mobile Exhibition to Open in South Shanghai on the 10th 75

Located at the Municipal Public Education Center on Wenmiao Road. Continued donations from various teams are still pouring in.

The Shanghai Solicitation Team Headquarters of the China Aviation Association, in order to deepen the public's understanding of aviation knowledge, held an aviation patriotism exhibition at the city stadium during the National Games. Although it lasted only ten days, it attracted two to three hundred thousand visitors. The headquarters, recognizing Shanghai's vastness and large population, decided to hold a mobile, simplified aviation patriotism exhibition, divided into five areas: South Shanghai, North Shanghai, West Shanghai, East Shanghai, and the Special District. The first exhibition will be set up at the Municipal Public Education Center on Wenmiao Road in South Shanghai and is scheduled to open on the 10th of this month. In addition to a systematic introduction of the headquarters' establishment process using photos and text, various airplane models and photographs have been collected, and explanations have been compiled for public viewing. Furthermore, a thatched shed has been built on a large plot of land inside the center. With the consent of the Naval Aircraft Manufacturing Plant, the Jiangfeng aircraft manufactured by the plant will be transported for display, and the manufacturing sequence of the aircraft and cross-sections of various components will be labeled and explained in detail, so that viewers can gain a concrete understanding of aviation knowledge.

Yesterday, the headquarters received 244 yuan in membership fees from Team Leader Jin Liren of Team 152, 24 yuan in membership fees from Team Leader Ding Shujing of Team 72, 90 yuan in donations from Team Leader Zhang Hongtu of Team 432, 50 yuan in membership fees from Deputy Team Leader Luo Yousheng of Team 250, 22.29 yuan in donations from Team Leader Tang Naikang of Team 343, 53 yuan in membership fees from Team Leader Huang Zhihe of Team 424, 40 yuan in membership fees from Team Leader Dong Zixing of Team 182, 30 yuan in membership fees from Team Leader Zhu Wenqi of Team 3, and 20 yuan in continued membership fees from Deputy Team Leader Shi Daochun of Team 67.

The Truth About the Xu Dawu Jumping Case Unveiled: 76

The Embarrassing Situation of Those Without Money for Prostitution. The Defendant Pimp Faces Charges of Coercing Murder.

Xu Dawu, a fortune-teller from Changzhou, whose business was named "Zhejiang Mo Huqi," and Zhong Yan, a local mute colleague, went to the Tianyunlou of the Wing On Company on the night of the 31st of last month to play. They enticed Li Xiuying and Wu Gendi, two waitresses from the fashionable theater, to the Lixing Inn at No. 341 Mintiniyin Road in the French Concession, opening rooms 5 and 8 to engage in illicit relations. They agreed to pay each woman three yuan the next morning. When the time came, they had no money to pay. The mute escaped first. The two women then called their pimps, Zhang Fusheng and Chen Yongxing, to come and reason with Xu, demanding payment. Xu, in desperation, jumped out of the window of the third floor of the Lixing Inn to escape, suffering a head injury and dying instantly. The inn reported to the police, who sent detectives to arrest the two women, Li and Wu, along with their pimps, Zhang and Chen. Xu's body was sent to the morgue for an autopsy. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. However, no family members of the deceased were found. Yesterday at noon, Judge Wang, a prosecutor from the Second Special Court, along with a forensic doctor and clerk, arrived at the morgue to examine the body. Qin Youyu, the detective in charge of the case, and Bao Tan Yao Zhupo, brought the four male and female defendants to the scene. After the judge and others finished the examination, they sat in court. Bao Tan first reported the case. Yu Shofu, the tea boy at the Lixing Inn, testified that Zhong Yan came first and stayed in the account room for two nights. Xu came on the night of the 28th, and they opened a room together. On the night of the 31st, Xu and the mute brought two women and opened rooms 5 and 8. The next morning, the mute got up and said he was going out for business, instructing me to get money from Xu. When I asked Xu for money, he had no money and tried to pawn his clothes, but he couldn't. So, Gendi went to call our men to demand payment. He said nothing. When a big man came, the deceased ran to the balcony and jumped down to his death. But I didn't see him jump. Li Xiuying testified that she was a waitress and didn't know the deceased or the person who escaped. They came for tea twice. That night, the two of them came to the Wing On Company for tea, giving us four jiao. At eleven o'clock, they asked Gendi and me to go out for refreshments, so we followed them to the inn. After eating, they asked us to stay overnight. We replied that our families were poor and that we needed money to stay overnight. They said they had eighty yuan deposited with the landlady (i.e., the innkeeper) and would take it out the next morning, giving each of us three yuan. We believed them. I slept with the deceased, and Gendi slept with the one who escaped. At seven o'clock yesterday morning, the one who escaped got up and said he was going out for business, instructing me to get money from the deceased. When I asked the deceased for money, he had no money and tried to pawn his clothes, but he couldn't. So, Gendi went to call our men to demand payment. He was silent and wanted to hit him, but I stopped him. Later, a big man came, and the deceased ran out to the balcony and jumped down to his death. But I didn't see him jump. Wu Gendi's testimony was the same as Li's. Zhang Fusheng and Chen Yongxing testified that Chen was in front, and Zhang was behind, going upstairs to ask the deceased to come downstairs to talk outside. There was no coercion or anything like that. After reviewing the testimonies, Prosecutor Wang determined that Xu Dawu had indeed died from a fall. The body was handed over to the Tongren Fuyuantang for photographs and burial. The defendants were investigated and handled by the police department. After the examination, the deceased was placed in a coffin by the charity. The defendants were taken back to the police station by the detectives to await prosecution and trial in the Second Special Court on Monday. It is said that the police will prosecute the defendants for coercing murder.

Reaction to Telephone Price Increase: Expert Committee Plans to Study Calculation Methods 78

Excessive Pricing for Extra Calls, Inappropriate Standards for Basic Calls.

Since the expert committee submitted the issue of the Shanghai Telephone Company's price increase to the Municipal Council, its summary has been published in various newspapers. Most users, such as shopkeepers and residents, have expressed dissatisfaction. A committee member from the Nanjing Road Citizens' Association issued an unofficial statement yesterday, intended for discussion among users throughout the city and for study by public organizations. The person said, "The Shanghai business environment is currently in a state of severe decline, and the social economy is also quite strained. This is not the time for a telephone price increase. Moreover, there are various reasons why the price should not be increased, as repeatedly pointed out in letters from the Chinese Taxpayers' Association, the Municipal Federation of General Chambers of Commerce, and this association to the Municipal Council and the expert committee, urging them to pay attention. (The reasons stated in the letters have been published in various newspapers, so we will set them aside for now.) Even if the calculation method proposed by the expert committee on a per-call basis could be somewhat accepted by users, the price standard and basic tier are still worthy of study. I will elaborate on three points: (1) Charging three cents for each call exceeding the basic tier is too high. Although commercial telephones vary in size and complexity, on average, each household makes at least twenty calls per day, requiring six hundred calls per month. In addition to the ten yuan for the basic 150 calls, adding 450 calls at three cents each amounts to 13.5 yuan, totaling 23.5 yuan. Compared to the previous price of 12.5 yuan per month, this is an increase of 88%. Even at one cent per call, the increase would be 16%. (2) The basic tier of 150 calls per month at ten yuan costs more than double the extra calls, charging over six cents per call. This standard is not very appropriate. Assuming that the extra calls are charged at three cents each, the basic tier should allow for thirty calls per day. (3) Assuming the basic tier is 300 calls at ten yuan, and each extra call is charged at one cent, the 600 calls per month mentioned earlier would incur an additional three yuan, totaling thirteen yuan. Compared to the previous price, this is an increase of 4%. With this method, users might be able to accept it, and the company would still increase its annual revenue by hundreds of thousands. Why be so insatiable? Moreover, someone who recently returned from London mentioned that the London Telephone Company is currently reducing its quarterly telephone fees from £1 12s 6d to £1 6s due to poor business conditions. Regional telephone fees have also been reduced from £1 7s 6d to £1. The prices for group services and business operations have also been reduced accordingly, averaging a 30% discount. With the high cost of living in London, telephone fees are being reduced. With the low cost of living in Shanghai, telephone fees are being increased. This reasoning is difficult to understand."

Xie Zhenyuan Invents Economical and Mobile "Sitings", Available in Electric and Coal Gas Versions 80

The Industrial Cooperative said that Xie Zhenyuan, director of the Ximolu branch of the China National Products Company, recognizing that although there are many types of modern heating appliances, most of them are quite expensive and complicated to operate, has invented two types of "economical and mobile Sitings" based on years of research, in order to save costs and suit hygiene purposes. One uses electricity, with an internal water storage device that stores an appropriate amount of clean water. The water is vaporized by electric heat, becoming a Siting. The other uses coal gas, with an internal device similar to the electric version, except that coal gas is used to burn the water tank, heating the water stored in the tank to vaporize it into a Siting. The height is 20 to 32 inches, and the width is calculated according to the number of tubes, with a minimum of 20 inches and a maximum of 30 inches. The thickness is 5 inches, and the base is equipped with four small wheels for free movement. The material is the latest type of four-tube Siting vapor band, with a delicate and beautiful design. Both the electricity and coal gas consumption are very economical, and the use is convenient. The price is low, truly meeting the principle of economy. It is understood that Xie has raised funds to establish the Shichun Factory to manufacture as much as possible to meet social needs.

Shanghai Public Security Bureau: Establishing Additional Drug Rehabilitation Hospital, Site Already Determined 82

Dagongshe reports that since the Shanghai Public Security Bureau began compulsory registration of smokers, the daily workload has doubled and intensified. The total number of registered smokers has now been tallied, reaching over 22,000. The establishment of an additional drug rehabilitation hospital has been agreed upon. Dagongshe reporters have investigated and reported the details below:

Statistics on the Total Number of Registered Smokers

The voluntary registration of smokers in this city began on July 1st and ended at the end of October. The total number of registered smokers, as announced by the Smoker Registration Section of the Public Security Bureau, is 19,934 over the past four months. Among them, 8,435 received general permits, 11,497 received permits for the poor, and 2 received travel permits. In addition, a total of 2,274 people applied for rehabilitation (the number from the Laobeimen branch has not yet been sent, and the branch has more than 2,000 people). 1,392 people have been sent for rehabilitation, 940 have been discharged after rehabilitation, 452 are currently undergoing rehabilitation, and 882 have not yet been sent for rehabilitation. The total number reaches 22,208. Together with the smokers from Laobeimen who have not been sent for rehabilitation, the total is approximately 25,000 people.

Agreed-Upon Measures for Establishing Additional Hospital

The bureau previously anticipated that the number of arrested smokers would be high after the start of compulsory registration. The existing hospitals in South Shanghai and North Shanghai were insufficient to meet the demand. In addition to temporarily borrowing a portion of the prisons of the Caohejing Jiangsu Second District Court to accommodate smoking offenders, it was planned to build a new hospital capable of accommodating 500 people. The municipal government ordered the Public Security Bureau and the Health Bureau to handle the matter jointly. At 9:00 AM yesterday, Dai, the section chief of the Narcotics Control Section of the Public Security Bureau, and Wu, the section chief of the First Section of the Health Bureau, met in the conference room of the Health Bureau to discuss the implementation. As a result, it was decided that building a new hospital would take too much time and would not be a permanent solution. There were already many smokers waiting for rehabilitation, and further delays would only increase congestion. In order to shorten the rehabilitation time, it was decided not to build a new hospital but to find and rent an empty building near the city center, large enough to accommodate 1,000 people. It has now been entrusted to Section Chief Wu to handle the matter. Once a suitable location is rented, an application will be submitted to the municipal government for approval, and the smokers applying for rehabilitation will be sent there.

Xinsheng News Agency reports that the Public Security Bureau's Chief of the Smoker Registration Section Dai Lizhen and the head of the Health Bureau Li Tingan decided yesterday morning at 10:00 AM to use the housing in the Jiangwan "Gaojing Memorial New Village" as the site for the temporary drug rehabilitation hospital. It is expected that the hospital can accommodate 1,000 smoking offenders. Public Security Bureau Chief Dai Lizhen also personally went to inspect the site and decided that the Health Bureau should prepare a document to submit to the municipal government for approval, and then repair the houses in the village to officially transform it into a temporary drug rehabilitation hospital and begin to accommodate smoking offenders.

Resolution of the Dianchun Hall Case: The Dried Seafood Guild Returns to Office 83

After the Supreme Court confirmed that the sugar industry had a 50% ownership, while the construction and flower industries, along with the foreign goods industry (i.e., the dried seafood industry), each held 25% ownership, misunderstandings were resolved and harmony was restored. It is now reported that the Dried Seafood Guild, due to its increasingly busy affairs, found its rented premises on Zhoushan Road in the French Concession insufficient. Consequently, the guild moved back to Dianchun Hall a few days ago to resume its operations.

Chinese Travel Agency Hangzhou Branch Organizes Tourist Groups

The Hangzhou branch of the China Travel Agency has recently organized tourist groups to Zhuji Luoluo Village, Jinhua Beishan, and Qililong, among other places. The following is a summary of the regulations:

(1) Dates: November 10th to 12th.

(2) Limit: 20 people. If less than half the number is reached, the trip may be canceled.

(3) Hospitality: The agency will dispatch a specialist to accompany and take care of the group.

(4) Costs: Each person will be charged 18 yuan, including train tickets, rickshaw, mountain sedan,游船食宿等費用(火車三等,輪船二等).

(5) Registration: Register with the agency starting immediately, closing at 8 PM on November 9th.

(6) Bring: Binoculars, cameras, walking sticks, flashlights.

(7) Itinerary: On November 10th, gather at the agency at 7 AM, cross the river, and take the 9 AM train from the riverside station to Zhuji. Arrive in Zhuji at 11:21 AM and take a rickshaw to visit Luoluo Village and the Xishi Temple. At 5:20 PM, take the train from Zhuji Station to Jinhua and stay at the agency's hostel. On November 11th, at 7 AM, take a mountain sedan to visit Beishan. At 10 AM, arrive at Dongqian Village and visit the Shuanglong Cave, Binghu Cave, and Chaozhen Cave. Have lunch at the Jinhua Temple. At 1 PM, take a mountain sedan to Zhuma Hall and take the 4:09 PM train to Lanxi. Arrive at 4:40 PM and visit the Lanxi streets. Have dinner at Chuanyuan Tower at 6 PM. Leave Lanxi by boat and spend the night on the boat. On November 12th, arrive at Yandongguan at 6 AM, follow Qililong to Tonglu, and transfer to a boat back to Hangzhou. Arrive in Hangzhou around 5:30 PM.

It is said that people in this city who want to participate can first contact the travel department of the head office at No. 420 Sichuan Road to register.

Children's Bookstore Prepares to Expand, Re-elect Directors and Supervisors... Increase Capital

Since its establishment, the business of Children's Bookstore Co., Ltd. has been growing year by year. It is learned that the term of office of the company's directors and supervisors has expired, and an extraordinary shareholders meeting was held a few days ago. As a result of the re-election, Pan Gongzhan, Wu Guochang, Ni Gang, Zhang Yiqu, Shi Zhikun, Song Yunlong, and Yan Fang were elected as directors, and Shao Xunru, Xu Zuoliang, and Mao Fengzhi were elected as supervisors. The shareholders' meeting also resolved to allow an increase in capital from 50,000 yuan to 200,000 yuan to expand the business, which will be planned and implemented by the board of directors. Yesterday at 4 PM, the company held a joint meeting of directors and supervisors, and Pan Gongzhan was elected as chairman of the board. In accordance with the resolution of the shareholders' meeting, it was decided to first increase the new capital by 80,000 yuan as a preliminary plan for development, and the subscription will begin immediately, closing at the end of February of the 25th year.

Chinese and Foreign Charity Relief Association Disaster Relief

The Chinese and Foreign Charity Relief Association on Renji Road recently received a report from the Peixian branch regarding disaster relief efforts. The report stated that the disaster situation in the county was extremely severe, as previously reported. In the Binhu area, disaster victims were everywhere. A previous request for 5,200 yuan for disaster relief was granted, but it was like a drop in the bucket. Since the beginning of autumn, the Yellow River has been surging dramatically. Another request for 5,000 yuan was granted to Peixian, but before it could be investigated and distributed, the Xiaosiduan levee broke, and the disaster area suddenly increased. The sixth and seventh districts were completely submerged, and most of the first and second districts were also flooded. At that time, they were busy building protective embankments and providing emergency relief. Before one wave subsided, another arose. On the night of the 24th of this month, a strong wind and heavy rain struck, and the Gaoxiaohu levee suddenly collapsed again. The water flowed rapidly, and the Yellow River surrounded the city in all directions within an hour. Currently, the disaster area has expanded further. The sixth and seventh districts have become a vast swamp, and most of the first and second districts are submerged. Part of the fifth district is also submerged. The water is rising daily, and the number of disaster victims is increasing. According to a recent survey in the sixth and seventh districts, the number of disaster victims has reached over 6,000. The previously received 5,000 yuan is a very small amount and difficult to distribute. Recently, the work of protecting the city has been urgent, and the first, second, and fifth districts have not yet been surveyed. In this situation, it is impossible to start distribution without requesting a large sum of money. It is requested that a large sum of money be approved for early investigation and distribution to save the disaster victims, and that a number of cotton-padded clothes be allocated to help the disaster victims keep warm.

Publication of Feng Menglong's Mountain Songs, Published by Chuanjing Tang in Penglai Market

Feng Menglong of the Ming Dynasty was a famous scholar in Jiangsu. He wrote a type of mountain song called "Tong Chi Er Nong," totaling ten volumes. All the songs collected are folk songs, which can be used to examine the language and customs of that time. The Chuanjing Tang Bookstore in Penglai Market in this city has obtained a Ming Dynasty engraved version, typeset in imitation Song typeface into a thick volume, with new-style punctuation. It includes prefaces and postscripts by Gu Jiegang, Qian Nanyang, and others. It sells for eight jiao and is quite popular for a time.

Free Smallpox Vaccination at Two Hospitals in Tilanqiao

Du Yuesheng, Wang Yiting, Liu Hongsheng, Cui Youqing, Wang Boyuan, and others, the founders of the Hongkou Civilian Obstetrics Hospital and the Chinese Hospital, care about the common people. As winter approaches, to prevent smallpox, they are providing free smallpox vaccinations at the hospital behind the Tilanqiao Police Station. In addition to obstetrics, gynecology, internal medicine, pediatrics, and smoking cessation departments, the hospital also has an infant care unit with multiple nannies, specializing in caring for infants of impoverished women using new methods of childcare.

Crime Statistics for Last Week

The Municipal Public Security Bureau announced that a total of 324 criminal cases occurred within the city in the past week. A total of 562 suspects, both male and female, were arrested. The breakdown is as follows: 18 robbery cases with 20 suspects, 93 theft cases with 144 suspects, 70 assault cases with 140 suspects, 33 abduction cases with 62 suspects, 9 opium/morphine cases with 14 suspects, 8 gambling cases with 41 suspects, 18 fraud cases with 24 suspects, 3 communist party cases with 9 suspects, 3 murder cases with 5 suspects, 9 arson cases with 13 suspects, 3 counterfeit currency cases with 3 suspects, 9 cases of violating police regulations with 21 suspects, and 48 other criminal cases with 66 suspects. A total of 324 cases and 562 suspects. All the suspects arrested have been preliminarily interrogated by the Third Section. Except for 123 cases that were minor and dealt with according to the regulations for violating police rules or sentenced to release, the remaining suspects have been sent to the local court or other competent authorities for trial. The number of criminal cases and suspects arrested this week increased by 49 and 880, respectively, compared to last week.

Woolen Fabric Industry Announces Price Increase

The Woolen Fabric Guild announced yesterday that recently, due to the sharp rise in gold prices and the drastic shrinkage of foreign exchange, the cost of imported goods has suddenly increased by 20% to 30% compared to before. If the selling price is not slightly increased, it will be difficult to avoid losses. Therefore, the guild has decided to temporarily increase the prices of all kinds of woolen fabrics by a minimum of 10% from now on. As this concerns costs, a public announcement is made in the newspaper for your information.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the area around Shandong and the Yellow Sea would be cloudy with showers and strong cyclones due to the passage of a low-pressure system moving northeast or east-northeast. Educational News

Ministry of Education Statistics on the General Situation of Primary Education in the Country

According to the Ministry of Education's statistics on various types of education, in general, higher education, secondary education, primary education, and social education have all been counted up to the 23rd year. However, the overall detailed classification statistics of each county and city directly under the jurisdiction of various departments and bureaus, because each department first investigates and collects each province and city (cities are easier, provinces have six or seventy counties, or even more than a hundred counties, so the circulation is repeated and time-consuming, and it is difficult to complete in a short period of time), circulation, It is difficult to report in detail for a while, and it is even more difficult to collect the remote provinces for a while. Therefore, the Ministry of Education's statistics on primary education in primary and secondary schools, in addition to the general statistics for each year after the 20th year that have been prepared, detailed classification statistics are either being printed or being sorted out, and the essentials of the national primary education statistics for the 20th year that have been released by the Ministry are briefly described below.

(1) The number of primary education schools in the country in the 20th year was 259,863. In terms of type, there were 829 kindergartens, 238,393 primary schools, 19,835 senior primary schools, and 806 other schools. In terms of establishment, there were 5 national schools, 1,329 provincial and municipal schools, 60,439 county and municipal schools, 137,219 district schools, and 60,871 private schools.

(2) There were a total of 612,185 classes, including 1,318 kindergarten classes, 554,809 primary school classes, 54,892 senior primary school classes, and 1,166 other classes.

(3) The total number of children was 11,720,596, including 36,770 kindergarten students, 10,162,297 primary school students, 1,496,278 senior primary school students, and 25,251 other school students. By gender, there were 9,961,198 boys, accounting for 84.9%, and 1,759,398 girls, accounting for 15.1%.

(4) There were 546,032 teachers and staff, including 1,839 in kindergartens, 451,891 in primary schools, 90,439 in senior primary schools, and 1,863 others. There were a total of 506,804 men, accounting for 92.8%, and 39,228 women, accounting for 7.2%.

(5) The total expenditure was 93,625,513.73 yuan, with 61,045.77 yuan for kindergartens,

Page 20

Although the farmers are very busy, they are very happy. They play the violin and sing joyful songs. When it's time to rest, the young men and women dance, very joyfully. This kind of scene cannot be seen everywhere now, but in places like Transylvania, it is still seen.

There are also many interesting customs here during the wheat harvest. For example, during the harvest period, if the landlord comes to the fields, the most beautiful maiden among the harvesters must immediately stop working and tie him up with a rope made of wheat leaves. Then the maiden asks the landlord for a certain amount of ransom money. She will never untie the rope until she receives a considerable price. This kind of ransom money used to be dozens of Pengő, but now it is a few kilograms of fine wine. It is said that this is done so that the wheat will not fall off the ears. At the same time, during the harvest, the first and last ears of wheat have significant religious meaning. The first ear of wheat to be cut is cut by a child symbolizing fertility. After cutting, it is erected into a cross and offered to the angels, thus worshipping it as a destroyer of demons. As for the last ear of wheat, it is left for the rats, wild birds, and demons. In addition, the poor can also get a little favor here. In some places, the farmers make the leftover ears of wheat into a human figure, decorate it with flowers, and dance around it.

In some parts of Hungary, during the wheat harvest season, we also saw such a strange thing: the farmers made wreaths out of cut wheat sheaves and transported them to the landlord's house. During this time, the harvesters walked, singing and dancing, and the women all wore white clothes or other gorgeous costumes, carrying bouquets of flowers together. In Transylvania, the farmers piled the cut wheat sheaves on carts, and then used wheat ears and wild flowers to make a beautiful big arch on the cart. They also found the most beautiful virgin who was not afraid of cold water to stand in the middle of it. Then they formed a line and drove to the landlord's house. When they passed in front of each farmhouse, people poured cold water on the beautiful woman on the cart. This brings a rich harvest. When the procession arrived at the landlord's house, the landlord gave the farmers some gifts, and the farmers offered him this kind of poem:

"The harvest is over,

The affectionate master now welcomes us,

We hurry to participate.

We must offer fragrant wreaths!

We use beautiful garden flowers and wildflowers,

To tie a lovely wreath of wheat ears;

For the master, we bring it here,

To participate in the master's harvest thanksgiving!

God, please give us lasting years,

Please give our couple a lasting life!

Our couple is as harmonious as a pair of doves!"

After this ceremonial exchange, a grand feast and dance began. They drank under the clear sky until dawn.

When the grape harvest season comes, the Hungarians are of course very busy, but at this time they show infinite joy. They forget all their pain and sorrow, and they want to drink recklessly. There is a popular saying here: "A grape harvest without wine and entertainment is like a wedding without music." From this, one can imagine the joy of the Hungarians during the grape harvest season.

The Hungarian vineyards have volcanic soil, which is more suitable for cultivating grapes than anywhere else in the world. The grapes produced here can be made into the famous golden grape wine, which is said to bring the dead back to life after drinking it. In addition, there are several other types of wine that are also very precious. Therefore, Hungarians cherish their produce very much. This treasure is their panacea for dispelling worries.

Hungarian weddings are mostly held at the end of the grape harvest. They celebrate the wedding with gifts that cannot be separated from new wheat bread and new wine. Here is a little song:

"The virgin who first sees the red grapes,

Will surely marry in the autumn."

This is a demonstration of the relationship between Hungarian weddings and grapes, and it is also a manifestation of their cherishing of grapes.

When the harvest of large vineyards is over, just like during the wheat harvest, Hungarians also sing, dance, and revel. The girls also wear white clothes, decorated with beautiful wild flower crowns, to participate in this joyful performance.

Occasional Chats on the Hegemonic War Between Britain and the United States by Ju Xiao

Which is ultimately the leading and strongest country in the world? This is the reason for the contradictions between the imperialists in the world, and it is also the eternal problem between Britain and the United States.

Since the United States is swaying on the world political stage under the guise of peace, it is naturally impossible to openly propose the slogan of re-dividing the world. But it cleverly used the "open door policy pill, coated with a layer of sweet sugar, to compete with Britain, France, and other countries for economic power. The so-called open door policy means that the United States can use capital to join the aggression with equal rights in all exclusively occupied colonial areas. After this brilliant plan is realized, the power to rule the colonies will become a hollow formality, while the claws of American capital, relying on their strong strength, will actually occupy the position of economic power.

Canada is the best example. Although it formally belongs to Britain, it is economically no different from the United States.

As for the king of the sea, it should naturally belong to Britain, but how can the United States not devote all its efforts to the naval competition issue? Under the cover of peaceful lies, the United States once said to Britain: "Regardless of whether you agree that your warship tonnage does not exceed mine, if we ever start an arms race, you are afraid that you will not be able to outrun me no matter what." At that time, Britain was thinking of getting help from the United States to stabilize its finances, and everyone could not risk openly competing to build warships, wasting countless amounts of money in vain, so the principle of Two Powers Standard was established.

But although Britain swallowed its anger, it was determined not to remain silent. It would never easily let go of its hegemonic position. It tried its best to engage in the new development of military supplies, making the value of large battleships more than doubled than before. Also, since there was no limit on small warships, it maintained its maritime hegemony at all costs as much as possible. The failure of the Geneva Naval Disarmament Conference was as natural as water flowing into a channel. It could not be forced.

Their competition in military affairs is full of intrigue at all times. Let's observe the situation as follows: Apart from the Hawaiian Islands, the United States has very few naval bases, so it needs large cruisers to threaten combat warships (armored and gunned merchant ships in wartime). As for Britain, because it has many connecting naval bases, it does not need overly large cruisers, but needs light and flexible warships to protect commerce and control commercial navigation. It can select good ships from its original powerful transport fleet at any time, arm them, and make them large cruisers. This kind of preparation has already been prepared in peacetime. Furthermore, the training of sailors is much better in Britain than in the United States. Therefore, even if the United States builds warships on a large scale immediately, it will not be able to catch up in time.

Later, the military agreement between Britain and France gave the United States a serious demonstration significance. The organized understanding and cooperation between Britain and France greatly disappointed the United States in its enthusiasm for ordering large warships. Although some people believe that the Anglo-French agreement was Britain's surrender to French militarism, sacrificing the Locarno peace policy, Louis George believes that it was the most glorious event in British diplomatic history after the war.

At present, the contradiction between Britain and the United States is becoming more and more serious every day. This can be proved by the fact that the US warship construction program has been approved by the Senate. Needless to say, the center of future competition is still the hegemonic issue of capitalist countries.

Miscellaneous Nocturne by Zhong

Christmas, Christmas in the South. With a heavy heart full of homesickness, I followed my classmate Lao Cheng, lazily trampling on the winter sunset, until we finally reached the front of a small gray Western-style house. Pushing open the small door of the fence, I could hear the clear sound of a piano inside. The living room was decorated very neatly, with a slightly gentle French flavor. In front of the glass window, a girl of seventeen or eighteen was playing the piano, wearing a green cheongsam, her hair blacker than charcoal. This was Lao Cheng's sister, Mingzhu.

Hearing the rough footsteps of a man, she turned her head as agile as a cat. Her pale olive-shaped face, worried eyes, and slender hands were still playing Chopin's "Nocturne." The somber and desolate piano sound flew out of the open small window, slipping into the dim Christmas evening sky. Lao Cheng told me that she had recently lost her love.

I looked at her worried, tired, but peaceful eyes—the depths of her eyes were a mystery that young people could not understand. That's how we met. In her eyes, I might just be a very ordinary young man, but in my eyes, she had such an amazing charm!

The next day, I ran all over the bookstores in the city to find a beautiful and meaningful New Year's card to send to her. After searching for a long time, I finally found one that was relatively satisfactory. Then I personally ran to the post office to mail it. When I came back, I felt a lot lighter. It felt like there was no lead block pressing heavily on my heart. However, the feeling of being relaxed did not last long, because I was worried about her reply again. Several times, I hid from my friends and circled around her house alone, feeling both scared and anxious in my heart, and my pace always became unnaturally fast. Sometimes there was piano music, and I really hoped that she would stick her head out from behind the fluttering white curtains. Sometimes there wasn't even piano music, and I worried that she was sick or something...

On the last day of that year, a misty winter morning, I finally received a light blue letter from the old postman. The envelope had delicate female handwriting on it. I felt like my heart was about to jump into my throat. Hiding from my classmates, I ran alone to a small path covered with fallen leaves. After running blindly for a while, I finally picked a very quiet place to sit down.

Her New Year's card was a landscape painting, with a bit of the scent of cosmetics. I stared at those slanted, feminine, small characters in blue ink. I felt like I was the happiest person in the world. The card showed the scenery of a winter sunset in Northern Europe. Snow was piled up on the streets, bridges, roofs, and branches. The Stone Bridge Emperor was an old small church. The windows of the church revealed brilliant lights, and behind the church was a crimson sunset. The tone of this painting was unusually somber. It could easily make people feel the weariness of life. A seventeen or eighteen-year-old girl, a medicine-like girl, really shouldn't use such a somber landscape painting to send to her boyfriend! However, at that time, I still felt unusually happy.

After that, I went to her house twice more. Everyone became a little more familiar, and talking became more natural. During that winter vacation, I returned to my hometown. After several nights of insomnia, I finally mustered up the courage to write the first letter to her. A week later, she replied with a short letter. Although it was such a short letter, it stirred up my infinite emotions. So I wrote the second letter, the third letter...

In the spring, school started, and I rushed back to S City like an arrow. As soon as I arrived in S City, I entrusted my luggage to my classmates to take care of, and again hired a car to go to her house alone. At this time, it was early spring in southern Fujian. Everything was filled with a gentle spring mood. The verdant branches of the street trees, the laughter of children, the shadows of the spring sun, and the new store windows all made me feel as if I was in a beautiful dream on a summer night.

Getting out of the car, I gently knocked on the door of her house with trembling hands. It was her seven or eight-year-old younger brother who came to open the door, his black and shiny eyes wide open, playfully shaking his head. I didn't understand what he meant. An odd incense was burning in the living room, and a light blue smoke circled out of the clean glass window. A woman's head stretched out from the study, it was her mother, followed by a chili-like wry smile. She said Lao Cheng was not at home, and her voice was a bit choked up. Then I suddenly felt that the living room was much emptier than before. In front of the glass window was still that black piano, with a layer of dust covering the lid.

She had passed away two days ago from acute pneumonia. She, a withered flower, did not have unlimited attachment to life, and death was just a quiet rest. But for me, how could I forget her cat-like head, pale face, dark black hair, tired and worried eyes! So, every time I heard Chopin's "Nocturne," my eyes were always filled with tears like a child's.

A Discussion on Training and Cultivation: Saying "Turning Back" by Chao Fan

To press on with a stiff neck and advance bravely is a hero; to shrink back and hesitate is a coward. This is a common proverb used to encourage others to be capable and persevering in doing things, not to hesitate or give up halfway, and not to turn back midway. Indeed, if a person lacks a brave and resolute spirit in doing things, and turns back halfway, unwilling to go to the end, then his life's work will always be abandoned halfway and he will achieve nothing. Because of this, the two words "turn back" are the worst in this case. They represent a kind of indecisive bravery, a lack of forcefulness, and an action that is not adopted by any tough guy with responsibility and courage.

However, we often hear people say "Turning back is the shore" [i.e., repenting brings salvation]. This sentence originates from religion. It teaches people to abandon evil and return to righteousness, to abandon evil and follow good. Therefore, in one turn back, you can become a Buddha from a sinner, and jump from hell to heaven. So this sentence is originally superstitious in its original meaning, because becoming a Buddha is fundamentally a fantasy. There is no such thing as a Buddha in the human world or in heaven. Even if you turn back a thousand or ten thousand times, you will not become a Buddha. Even though this is said, it has become a habit of persuading people to reform and start anew in general secular language. This means that people cannot be without fault. "To correct mistakes is the greatest good." If a person is doing wrong and bad things, and also has to press on with a stiff neck and act recklessly, then this cannot be regarded as a hero, but only as continuing to degenerate and being beyond redemption, which is harmful to yourself, your country, and society. Moreover, in this case, the more courageous you are to turn back, the better, because only the wise can make the darkness turn to light between breaths; only heroes can have the courage not to cover up their shortcomings or hide their faults. In this case, turning back is not only a proper and good behavior, but also something that only a tough guy can do, because resolutely reforming and starting anew also requires the greatest courage and boldness.

The above two points are the ways that ordinary people use the word "turn back" to predict future actions. When examining past actions, people also commonly use the word "turn back," and it also has both positive and negative meanings. When many people reflect on the past, they often sigh, "Past events are unbearable to recall." The word "recall" is an elegant way of using the word "turn back," which goes without saying. People often sigh that "it is unbearable to recall," which is a term to express a feeling of sentimentalizing the past. Either they feel that the present is not as good as the past, or they feel that the past is not as good as the present. When a person was previously in a smooth and lucky situation, but now has returned to desolation and decline, they sigh "it is unbearable to recall" when feeling that good dreams do not last forever. Conversely, when a person has done many bad things in the past, wasted their years and wasted their energy and money, and has spent their precious life in vain, when they finally wake up, they also sigh that "it is unbearable to recall." Therefore, when people turn back to look at their history, they either admire or hate it. This will naturally lead them to evaluate and review their past.

Page 21

The review of past life is a guide for a new life in the future. This is true for personal review, and it should also be true for social movements. The future success of many great social reformers or transformers is based on a strict review of past gains and losses. Without old lessons to enrich our experience and guide our future activities, we will not be able to recognize the objective overall development trend. Therefore, those great social reformers or transformers not only often turn back to review history themselves, but also often teach people to turn back to history, to review the development of history, in order to determine future activities. In this way, whether it is for the individual, the country, or society, turning back to history in order to gain experience and lessons, and turning back to carefully examine the gains and losses of the past, has absolute significance for the progress of mankind and the development of a new life. And no matter what the result of your turning back is, whether you give a good or bad evaluation of the past, it is necessary as long as you are gaining lessons.

However, there are also people in society who, when they turn back to look at old history, do not focus on gaining historical lessons, but are instead intoxicated by old traces, or stop moving forward, or even follow history back, which has the opposite result from the above-mentioned turning back to past history, and becomes a turn back that hinders the evolution of mankind. Turning back is anti-evolution. This kind of turning back is not needed by mankind.

We humans live in living events. In the complex events and endlessly changing environments, engaging in life's struggles cannot mechanically adopt a fixed way of acting. We cannot say that we should never turn back in any situation. If the cause we are working hard for clearly has a smooth road to success ahead, and victory is already in sight, but at this time, we are blocked by some obstacles that can be overcome, and we retreat in fear of difficulty, adopting a method of turning back, then that possible success will be transformed by you into failure. In this case, turning back is not a blessing but a disaster. Conversely, if there is clearly a dead end ahead of us, and no matter how hard we try to rush forward, there will only be a destined result of failure, then if we do not know how to turn back, and still bury our heads and squeeze forward regardless, the result will naturally only be like a rat disturbing a cow's horn, the more you disturb, the tighter it becomes, and there is no way out, and you will end up hitting the wall and suffering a bloody sacrifice in vain. This is just like fighting between two armies. If the enemy's formation has already shown signs of collapse, but you do not have the courage to advance, but are turning back and looking around, or even thinking about turning back and running away, then not only will you have no victory to gain, but you will be defeated under the enemy's counterattack. Also, if strategically speaking, you should retreat, then you should turn back and retreat very quickly at this time. If not, and you still press on with a stiff neck, or hesitate and refuse to turn back and retreat, the result will either be the annihilation of the entire army, or you will be surrounded by the enemy. Mankind is the same on the battle line of life.

In short, not all turning back is good or bad, nor is all not turning back good or bad. In terms of avoiding failure, correcting mistakes, and obtaining past lessons, turning back of all kinds is appropriate and correct. But in terms of striving for possible victory and not making oneself a laggard in the times, not turning back of all kinds is correct and appropriate. Therefore, we can only decide whether to turn back or not based on the nature of the complex situation and the changes in the circumstances.

International Intelligence: American Industry and Commerce by Se Ying

The United States of America, which has the nickname "Kingdom of Gold," could not help but tremble uneasily on its throne at a time when the world was suffering from an economic recession. As a result, President Hoover lost the opportunity to be re-elected and left the White House sadly. Although President Roosevelt was good at maneuvering, each "brain trust" that he pulled out of his sleeve became like dew under the morning sun, and less than one in ten achieved practical results.

It is undeniable that American industry and commerce once emitted a glorious splendor that would last for thousands of years. But their economists could not deeply observe the progress of the American economy and predict the future trend of this industry and commerce. The endless production finally ended in a complete defeat. We only need to look at the party of monopoly capital—the Republican Party—which, in the previous election, had no political program, but only the slogan "Good for everyone" to connect small bourgeois, farmers, and the electorate of the working class, to believe this.

The economic state of the United States has almost certain panic centers. The most important are the automobile industry, the coal industry, the oil industry, the construction industry, various installment payment businesses, and securities speculation. In the automobile industry, there will inevitably come a day of overproduction. The Ford Company alone can produce 2.5 million cars per year, but its competitors are also maximizing their production capacity and producing cheap cars as much as possible. General Motors Company "caught up" in front, and other medium-sized car companies "followed closely" behind. As a result, the total capacity of American car factories is at least six million vehicles per year. As a result of such fierce competition, small and medium-sized car factories will inevitably be defeated. The tragedies and tragedies of business wars seem to be staged in the same way.

There is also an oversupply in coal production. In 1928, although there was a major miners' strike and the output dropped slightly, there was no slight decrease in stockpiles. Afterwards, the sharp overproduction crisis became unmanageable.

The oil industry has the same fate. The daily production of oil is still 2.4 million barrels. The inventory in the stacks is accumulating day by day, and it is now sufficient for the whole country for one year. Prices tend to fall, and a crisis is almost inevitable.

Because of the weakness of the purchasing power of the entire world market, overproduction, and a large number of unemployed workers are as prevalent as the flu, which makes installment payment operators lose their business reliance. Because unemployed workers and employees have no way to purchase these household, vehicle, clothing, and other supplies, the financial position of financial enterprises that invested in this type of business is put at risk.

Speculation in the stock exchange is also very prevalent. Four or five million shares are traded on the New York Stock Exchange in one day, and the price fluctuations are extremely large. This kind of securities trading... trend.

In addition to these crisis elements, the American agricultural panic is also in a constant state, and it will go to the next level. As for the working class, Bowers has a million completely unemployed workers and three million part-time workers. According to accurate statistics, there are between 5.6 million and 8 million unemployed people. At present, agriculture and mining are both deliberately reducing workers. Commerce, the automobile industry, and the construction industry are also eliminating unskilled workers in order to rationalize.

Industry and commerce are in such a state... When will the business recovery come under the blue sky? Roosevelt spent a lot of effort, which is no different from a drunkard raising his hands to draw a big circle in the sky.

Literary Works: Extract from the Account Book (1) by Pu Yu

On the way.

Arriving at a thatched shop, the coachmen shouted, "Have a snack." As for me, I used official jargon to order them to pull the cart quickly. It turned out that these two bastards parked the cart and shouted in a low voice:

"We're hungry! Our bellies are made of flesh!"

Damn it! What's the big deal if you starve to death? It's no small matter to delay my official business!—But it's true that they can't run without filling their stomachs.

The food at the chicken shop is only fit for the lower classes—the stomachs of the coachmen. I almost vomited at the sight of it. What's hateful is that the ugly woman even asked:

"Does this master want to eat?"

Damn it, I really wanted to slap her. Fortunately, Jiang Xiwu helped me scold:

"You don't know how to speak properly. Do you think this food is fit for...?"

Before he could finish scolding, I took out a "Pao Tai" cigarette to calm my nerves. Just as I put it in my mouth, Lao Jiang quickly fumbled for a match. With a "scratch" sound, he lit it for me. This kid was so eager to please me that I felt embarrassed. I had no choice but to give him one. He stretched out both hands as if holding a holy decree, his face full of smiles:

"Thank you, Director!"

I exhaled a puff of smoke before replying with a "Hmm." Because the dignity of a superior cannot be taken lightly, I can only hide my love for him in my heart.

"Director, about the Yuan Tai Flour Mill matter, what exactly...?"

He hesitated to say the second half of the sentence, but I understood that he wanted to probe the truth. Is that possible? I was selected from among the best. So I put on a serious face and glared at him coldly:

"The Provincial Bureau has an order, and the Director also sent a telegram. Don't think wildly!" (To be continued)

Literary Works: Pharmacy by Mao Yannian

It is already the season for heatstroke, the season when "heatstroke" and "malaria" are prevalent. It is said that "when the weather is hot, the doctors never stop." In theory, it should be a time when doctors and pharmacies are "prospering." If it were in previous years—

"If it were in previous years," said Doctor Xia, "at that time, I would have been so busy that I couldn't breathe. Our pharmacy business would also be..."

"Who says no? I still remember it clearly: one day you saw twenty-five patients at the counter and went to the countryside to see four. You also sold fifty-two doses of medicine. Just the cash alone was a hundred strings of cash. At that time, at that time... um, um..." Doctor Xia's wife said with a bit of emotion, "At that time, not only was our business good, but other people's businesses were also..."

Indeed, at that time, not only was Doctor Xia's "Fuxing Hall" "prospering," but other people's businesses were also "prosperous." Even Wang the Monk, such a lousy doctor, and the lousy pharmacy he opened had many people seeing doctors and many people filling prescriptions. However, they could never catch up with Doctor Xia, because among the seven doctors and seven pharmacies in Liu Town, Doctor Xia was considered the most famous, and the "Fuxing Hall" signboard was considered the oldest. It is said that his grandfather once treated the emperor and cured his illness in the Imperial Hospital. The large plaque with the words "Merit Equal to the State Physician" that hangs in his house was bestowed by imperial decree. After the old imperial physician retired and returned to his hometown, he opened this pharmacy—"Fuxing Hall"—in Liu Town. Thus, one generation of small imperial physicians was passed down to the current Doctor Xia. Originally, Doctor Xia was also called "Imperial Physician" when he was first born, but later, after the Republic of China was established, he slowly changed his name to "Doctor." However, no matter how the name changed, Doctor Xia was still a "hereditary Confucian physician." As a result, many people came to see him, and the pharmacy business was especially good. Carriages came and went every day, very enthusiastically, very "prestigious"! However, most of the people who invited him were officials and gentlemen. As for the poor, because they were afraid that he would be arrogant and demand a lot of money, they usually didn't dare to invite him. They only mustered up their courage to invite him once or twice when they were seriously ill. Therefore, if Doctor Xia's sedan chair appeared in the villages of Liu Town, they knew that someone's illness was already very serious.

But in recent years, fewer and fewer people have invited Doctor Xia to see a doctor, and the medicine from "Fuxing Hall" has gradually become less "popular." As a result, Doctor Xia was confused and very anxious: "What is the reason for this? Could it be that all the patients have died!"

"Don't talk nonsense!" Doctor Xia's wife said disapprovingly, "There are many patients. I think it's because you're too arrogant. You have to take a sedan chair every time you go out. Think about it, when poor people get sick, they have to borrow a sedan chair to invite a doctor, prepare food and drink, pay for the consultation, and pay for the medicine. Where do they get so much money? I think you..."

Doctor Xia nodded and stroked his beard. Later, he really took the sedan chair less often, didn't eat the food of the poor, and didn't care much about the consultation fee. As a result, poor patients gradually came to invite him, and they also advertised to others: "Doctor Xia is good now, he doesn't demand too much."

But now that the summer season has arrived, I heard that many people returning to their hometowns are suffering from "malaria." Why are so few people inviting me to see a doctor? He paced slowly in the magic box room, holding a white copper water pipe in his left hand, and the paper twist in his right hand had an inch-long ash. His brows were furrowed tightly, as if it was difficult to figure out the reason. Finally, he suddenly said angrily: "Damn it, there are such strange things in the world: patients don't invite doctors, don't take medicine! I've been practicing medicine for thirty years, and I've never been like this before..."

He was about to say more when he suddenly saw the words "Sacred Medicine for Malaria" on the back cover of a book that his son was holding. Looking further down, he saw "Quinine." He couldn't help but feel angry and slammed the cigarette pipe heavily on the tea table. He cursed with force: "Damn it, what is this "sacred medicine"? I don't believe it can cure diseases!"

The son was startled and put down a "royal leg," sat up straight, rolled his eyes and looked at him. After a long time, he said, "What are you angry about, old man?"

"What? Look—" He took the book from his son's hand and pointed to the back cover, "Look, isn't this nonsense?"

The son then understood the reason for his anger, so he smiled and said:

"There's no need to get angry about this. However, many people now believe in Western medicine, and Western medicine is popular all over the country. Even our school has invited a Western doctor..."

"Humph!" The old man was even more angry, "You young people, after reading a few foreign books, you forget your roots. How can Western medicine be compared with Chinese medicine? Their diagnosis doesn't involve "looking, listening, asking, and feeling the pulse," and their use of drugs doesn't involve "yin and yang and the five elements." They don't distinguish between "ruler, minister, father, and son," and they can't even figure out the "heart, liver, spleen, and kidneys." How can they know what is called "pulse theory" and what is called "drug properties"? Not to mention the ancient sages and virtuous people, just take me as an example. I have treated countless dangerous and serious illnesses since I was born. If you were to encounter a Western doctor, it would be terrible! You should know that the medicine used by Western doctors is all "hegemonic," while Chinese medicine is "the king's way..."

"Okay, okay, take those words and tell them to the patients. You always have such an old temper, always saying how good you are, but other people insist on seeing a Western doctor. Look, the second wife of Jia on Heng Street didn't go to the city to live in the hospital after her ex-husband died? A few years ago, when the rich people in our town got sick, they almost all invited you to see them, but now they always like to find a Western doctor. I say..."

Before Doctor Xia's wife could finish speaking, Doctor Xia interrupted her and said, "You all say Western medicine is amazing, then I won't do this craft anymore! Is it okay to let the whole family starve to death?"

The son said, as if feeling embarrassed: "It's not that Western medicine is amazing, but many people believe in it, which has an impact on our business. At the same time, people are getting poorer day by day, and many don't have money to treat illnesses. They just endure it if they can."

The old man had nothing to say, but he was still very angry in his heart. He hated why some people wanted to see a Western doctor and why they didn't see a Chinese doctor. So he wanted to publicize the "mysterious and profound" aspects of Chinese medicine and expose the "nonsense" of Western medicine. Only in this way could he regain people's hearts and his business could improve. But what method should he use? After thinking about it, he couldn't come up with a plan. Finally, he suddenly remembered that people in the town often came to paste advertisements, publicizing the advantages and effects of certain Western doctors or medicines. That's right, the reason why Western medicine is trusted is because they know how to advertise. He can do this, so why can't I? So his heart relaxed and his eyes lit up. With a decisive attitude, he ordered his son, "Go and get me a few sheets of yellow paper for wrapping medicine."

Doctor Xia grinded the ink, dipped the brush, and waved it on the yellow paper... "Medicine is a benevolent art. Shi... Shennong tasted hundreds of herbs and learned about the properties of medicines, so he taught the people about medicine. Passed down to later generations, the principles are clear, and the skills are also refined. For example, Zhongjing's treatment of internal diseases and Hua Tuo's treatment of external diseases have the magical effect of reviving the dead. Are they lacking in the power of miraculous elixirs and immortal medicines? Until recent times, the world's customs have gradually changed, and people have forgotten their roots. They respect Western medicine as sacred and regard Western medicine as noble products. As a result, demons and heretics are scattered throughout China, and worthless things are spread in all directions. They don't know that Western medicine is unfamiliar with pulse theory and doesn't recognize the properties of medicines. In this way, with yin and yang not distinguished, how can diseases be cured? This hall has been a hereditary Confucian physician for generations, with secret family recipes. Moreover, my late father once served as an imperial physician and personally cured the emperor's illness. Since I was born, I have read the Materia Medica thoroughly. I have hung up my gourd (practiced medicine) for thirty years, and all the dangerous illnesses I have encountered have been cured with medicine. Recently, the summer heat is steaming, and diseases arise from it. I am mindful of the meaning of "medicine is a benevolent art." Those who are poor and come to see me will not be charged for medicine. Why not come!

Doctor Xia wrote five sheets with great enthusiasm, then shook his head and read them again. Then he looked at his son very proudly: "How do you think this compares to the advertisements of those Western pharmacies?"

"It's good," the son said with a smile, "But I'm afraid many people won't understand it."

"Don't understand? It's so thorough."

His son's words seemed to disappoint him a little, but he didn't mind. He instructed his apprentice to first wipe the plaque in the central hall and the wooden couplets on both sides clean (because the central hall is the place where wealthy people have their pulses taken), and then brush those small plaques hanging around the cabinet room, such as "Zhongjing's Legacy" and "Bian Que Reborn," and wash them. Taking advantage of the fact that today is a "slow market" (the market town where we are from calls the market day "dang chang" and peacetime "leng chang

Shanghai-Huai'an Long-Distance Telephone Service: Costing $1.50 per Call 84

A report from the East China News Agency states that the Ministry of Transportation's long-distance telephone project across nine provinces is progressing rapidly. Besides the Beijing-Tongzhou section, which is already in operation and connected to Shanghai, the Shanghai-Huai'an section (from Shanghai to Qingjiangpu) has now been fully installed and is officially operational. The cost for a three-minute call from Shanghai to Huai'an is $1.50. The Shanghai Telephone Bureau has already informed all retail outlets to take note.

Pudong Labor Village Celebrates Tenth Anniversary Yesterday 85

Chairman Lu Ganchen and others reported in great detail on the progress. Guests Zhu Maocheng and Chen Liting both gave speeches.

The Pudong Labor Village, established by the Labor Department of the Shanghai YMCA, held its tenth-anniversary celebration yesterday at 3:00 PM in the village's community center. Many guests were in attendance. Chairman Lu Ganchen reported on the Labor Village's undertakings in great detail. The details are recorded below:

A Gathering of Guests

Among the guests who attended yesterday were Chen Liting from Jin Cheng Bank, Chen Jingsheng from the International Trade Bureau, Zhu Maocheng from the Rickshaw Committee, Xi Kegong from the Central Mint, Tian Heqing from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, representatives from the Pudong Party and government organs, and students from Qingxin Middle School, totaling approximately 500 people. The YMCA specially arranged a small steamer at the Bund Customs Wharf to transport them, providing attentive service. The YMCA's Boy Scouts, together with police officers from the Public Security Bureau, took care of all arrangements.

Grand Opening Ceremony

At 3:00 PM, the commemorative ceremony began. Lu Ganchen, the General Secretary of the YMCA and Chairman, reported on the Labor Village's undertakings in great detail. Fu Qinghuai, a member of the Labor Village, then gave a brief history of the YMCA's labor efforts over the past ten years. Guests Zhu Maocheng and Chen Liting then gave speeches in succession. Finally, there was a variety show. The event concluded at around 6:00 PM.

County Land Bureau Continues Registration in Nine Townships 86

The Shanghai County Land Bureau will resume registration on the first of this month for nine townships in the first district: Wu Hui, He Xi, and Ziteng; in the second district: Tang Wan and Tang Chun; and in the third district: Di Shan, Xiao Zhong, Nan Fu, and Dong Lin. Notices have been sent to the respective district offices to select locations and establish registration sub-offices. The previously established Ma Qiao and Da Jiang registration sub-offices will be closed. The unfinished business of the five townships of Ma Qiao, Yu Tang, Yu Nan, and Sha, will be handled directly by the bureau. The Da and two townships will be handled by the Chen Xing registration sub-office. The county government is issuing a proclamation urging unregistered households to apply. It is also reported that the review of various supporting documents for registration applications from the eight townships of Bei Qiao, Da Shu, Yu Ji, San Gang, Sha Ji, Zi Zhu, Zhong An, Wu San in the third district has been completed. Notification letters have been filled out and sent to the third district office for distribution to the respective households. Those who receive the notification letters must bring their previous receipts to the bureau to retrieve their documents within ten days.
